1 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


City of E. St. Louis v. E. St. Louis Fin. Advisory Auth.


Docket No. 87076


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


188 Ill. 2d 474; 722 N.E.2d 1129; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 1627; 243 Ill. Dec. 60



December 16, 1999, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged an Illinois appellate court decision holding appellee financial authority was entitled to impose its own budget on appellant and had not acted in an arbitrary and capricious manner in rejecting appellant's budgets under the Financially Distressed City Law, 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8-12-1 et seq. (West 1996).


OVERVIEW: Appellant city passed an ordinance requesting it be designated a financially-distressed city pursuant to the Financially Distressed City Law, 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8-12-1 et seq. (West 1996). Appellant was designated a financially-distressed city. It submitted two 1998 budgets. Both were rejected. Appellee authority listed several reasons each budget was rejected. Appellee authority imposed its own budget; appellant objected. The trial court ruled appellee could impose its own budget and had not acted arbitrarily and capriciously in rejecting appellant's budgets. The appellate court affirmed. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held the plain language of the statute did not confer upon appellee the power to impose its own budget. The court also held appellee's rejections of the budgets were not arbitrary and capricious since its explanations were supported by the evidence and did not consider factors the legislature did not intend.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part because legislature did not give appellee financial authority the power to impose its own budget on appellant city, but appellee did not act in an arbitrary and capricious manner in rejecting appellant's 1998 budgets.

 

2 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cervantes


Docket No. 87229


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


189 Ill. 2d 80; 723 N.E.2d 265; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 1619; 243 Ill. Dec. 233



December 2, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended December 2, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal, Circuit Court. COUNTY: Kane. CASE NUMBERS: TR98CF140.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which held that the Safe Neighborhoods Law, Ill. Pub. L. No. 88-680, was unconstitutional because it did not comply with the single subject rule of the Ill. Const. art. IV § 8.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with gunrunning. Appellee filed a motion to dismiss the charge on the basis that the Safe Neighborhoods Law (Law),Ill. Pub. L. No. 88-680, which created the offense of gunrunning, did not comply with the single subject rule of the Ill. Const. art. IV § 8. The lower court found that the law violated the single subject rule. The single subject rule provided that bills should be confined to one subject in order to prevent the passage of legislation that, standing alone, would not have mustered the votes necessary for enactment. The court determined that the Safe Neighborhood Law, which provided for neighborhood safety, violated the single subject rule when the legislators attached provisions to the bill that concerned abuses of the Women Infants and Children (WIC) Vendor Management Act, 410 Ill. Comp. Stat. 255/1 et seq. (1992) and other provisions unrelated to neighborhood safety.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The law that provided for neighborhood safety violated the single subject rule of the state constitution when legislators attached provisions unrelated to neighborhood safety, such as abuses of welfare benefits.

 

3 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Chavda v. Wolak


Docket No. 86687


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


188 Ill. 2d 394; 721 N.E.2d 1137; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 1626; 242 Ill. Dec. 606



December 2, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. COUNTY: DuPage. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. John W. Darrah. CASE NUMBERS: TR98MR0383.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a judgment of the Du Page County Circuit Court (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees on appellants' declaratory judgment action seeking fee title to entire vacated portion of abutting municipal property.


OVERVIEW: Municipality proposed vacating a portion of a street. Appellants and appellees owned property abutting the proposed vacation. Municipality passed an ordinance requiring that appellants alone pay the property's fair market value. Thereafter, appellants filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration that, upon payment of compensation to its municipality, appellants would be entitled to receive fee title to the entire vacated portion of the abutting property. Summary judgment was awarded to appellees on their counterclaim alleging the statute authorizing the municipal ordinance violated the due process clause because it authorized a municipality to award title to only one of several abutting owners. The court reversed, holding that there was no constitutional defect in the relevant statute because the ordinance awarding title to one of several abutting property owners only had to bear a reasonable relationship to the public interest sought to be protected.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case was remanded; there was no constitutional defect in the contested statute because the municipal ordinance awarding title in vacated property to one of several abutting property owners bore a reasonable relationship to the public interest sought to be protected.

 

4 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tellez-Valencia


Docket Nos. 85524, 85532 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


188 Ill. 2d 523; 723 N.E.2d 223; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 1473; 243 Ill. Dec. 191



November 18, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Tellez-Valencia, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 321 (Ill., Jan. 31, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, Second District, Lake County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Raymond J. McKoski. CASE NUMBERS: AC2-97-0853, TR96CD2024. Appeal, Appellate Court, Fourth District, Vermilion County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Thomas J. Fahey. CASE NUMBERS: AC4-97-0413, TR96CF264.
People v. Tellez-Valencia, 295 Ill. App. 3d 122, 692 N.E.2d 407, 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 164, 229 Ill. Dec. 634 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 1998)
People v. Moore, 295 Ill. App. 3d 676, 694 N.E.2d 184, 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 265, 230 Ill. Dec. 553 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 1998)



DISPOSITION: No. 85524-Affirmed. No. 85532-Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal to resolve a conflict between Second District of Appellate Court (Illinois), which reversed a conviction, holding that the plaintiff state could not amend the charging instrument to change the name of the offense, and the Fourth District of Appellate Court, which, affirming an identical conviction, held the opposite.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants were charged with and convicted of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. After defendants' convictions, and while their appeals were pending, the court declared the statute under which they were convicted was unconstitutional. On appeal, both defendants argued that their convictions were invalid because they were based upon charging instruments that failed to state an offense. The Second District of the Appellate Court reversed the conviction of the first defendant, holding that only the grand jury could make a substantive change to the indictment. The Fourth District of the Appellate Court reached the opposite result, holding that plaintiff state could, effectively amending the indictment on appeal. The court affirmed the Second District and reversed the Fourth District. The amendment sought by plaintiff state to each defendant's charging instrument was to cure a substantive, not a formal, defect, and these amendments could not be made on appeal.


OUTCOME: Affirmed as to one defendant, reversed as to other; convictions could not be upheld because amendment sought by plaintiff state to each defendant's indictment was to cure a substantive, not a formal, defect, and these amendments could not be made on appeal.

 

5 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


Docket No. 86453


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


188 Ill. 2d 352; 721 N.E.2d 546; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 1477; 242 Ill. Dec. 267



November 18, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, Third District, Kankakee County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Clark E. Erickson. CASE NUMBERS: AC4-97-0388, TR96CF561.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted plaintiff State's petition for leave to appeal as a matter of right, 134 Ill. 2d R. 317, from the judgment of the Appellate Court, Third District, Kankakee County (Illinois), holding the sound amplification statute unconstitutional. Only defendant's conviction for illegal sound amplification was before the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated battery of a police officer and various traffic offenses, including illegal operation of a sound amplification system. Defendant was convicted of all charges and appealed, challenging the illegal sound amplification conviction on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional. The appellate court reversed the conviction for illegal sound amplification, holding that the sound amplification statute violated the first amendment by regulating speech based on content without a compelling state interest. Plaintiff State appealed, presenting in the appeal whether the statute was consistent with the first amendment to the United States Constitution. The court concluded that the Illinois sound amplification statute was a content-based regulation of expression. The statute's restriction did not apply equally to all types of amplified sound; therefore, the judgment of the appellate court, reversing defendant's conviction for illegal sound amplification, was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court reversing defendant's conviction for illegal sound amplification was affirmed because the Illinois sound amplification statute was found to be a content-based restriction on free expression, which violated the first amendment. The statute's restriction did not apply equally to all types of amplified sound.

 

6 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smith


Docket No. 86423


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


188 Ill. 2d 335; 721 N.E.2d 553; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 1478; 242 Ill. Dec. 274



November 18, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, Second District, Lake County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. John R. Goshgarian. CASE NUMBERS: AC2-97-0471, TR97CF291.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed a judgment of the appellate court affirming a decision of the trial court to start her trial in her absence, entered by the Second District Appellate Court of Illinois, in a case where she was charged with unlawful possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was arrested on a drug charge. She was advised of her trial date. The trial court admonished her about being present. The court cautioned that should her trial proceed in absentia, she would not be able to confront witnesses or assist her attorney. Defendant advised the court of a medical appointment she had on the same date. The trial court determined the trial would be finished before her appointment. Defendant was absent when the trial started. The trial court proceeded against defendant in absentia after the state presented a prima facie case defendant was willfully absent. Defendant arrived 35 minutes late. She said her daughter had been late. She was convicted. The appellate court affirmed. On appeal, the court held defendant did not rebut plaintiff State's prima facie case that she was willfully absent because she did not show her absence was not her fault or beyond her control.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the appellate court affirmed because plaintiff State established a prima facie case of criminal defendant's willful absence from trial and defendant introduced no evidence to rebut plaintiff's case to show that her absence was not her fault or due to circumstances beyond her control.

 

7 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wooters


Docket No. 83595


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


188 Ill. 2d 500; 722 N.E.2d 1102; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 1480; 243 Ill. Dec. 33



November 18, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 12, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal, Circuit Court, Marion County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Patrick J. Hitpass. CASE NUMBERS: TR96CF88.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review from the Circuit Court, Marion County (Illinois), judgment that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) (West 1998) was unconstitutional, arising out of a trial of appellee for murdering her infant son.


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, the circuit court of Marion County (Illinois) convicted defendant of murdering her infant son. 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) (West 1998) prescribed mandatory life imprisonment for any person 17 years or older convicted of murdering a child less than 12 years old, provided the offender is not sentenced to death. The State did not seek the death penalty for defendant, and the circuit court refused to sentence defendant to a life term in prison. The circuit court ruled that section 5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) violated Ill. Const. of 1970 art. I, § 11, because it prevents the sentencing court from assessing any evidence that would mitigate against a term of natural life in prison. The court subsequently sentenced defendant to 25 years' imprisonment. The State appealed directly to the Supreme Court of Illinois. The court agreed with the legislature's determination that the murder of a child under age 12 by an individual age 17 or older warranted life imprisonment. However, the court affirmed the 25-year sentence imposed by the circuit court on the sole basis that the statute violated the single subject clause of the Ill. Const. 1970, art. IV, § 8.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the 25-year sentence imposed by the circuit court on the sole basis that the statute violated the single subject clause of the Illinois Constitution.

 

8 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. Farmers Ins. Group


Docket No. 84208


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


188 Ill. 2d 168; 720 N.E.2d 1052; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 974; 242 Ill. Dec. 97



October 21, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court, Third District, of Tazewell County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Donald C. Courson. CASE NUMBERS: AC3-96-0739, TR95L298.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the appellate court (Illinois), which found part of 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/143a (West 1996) to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff initiated action, seeking a declaration that the arbitration requirement in the uninsured-motorist portion of the automobile insurance policy issued to her by the defendant was unenforceable. The arbitration requirement was mandated by statute, as was a provision permitting either party to reject awards greater than $ 20,000, but made awards below that amount binding. The trial court dismissed the complaint, but the appellate court reversed, finding the statute unconstitutional for impairment of insured's right to contract. On appeal, the court held that the challenged provision did not violate public policy, because legislation itself is an expression of public policy. Further, the statute did not impair an existing contract, negating a contract clause claim. Finally, the court found a rational relation of the statute to its purpose, and thus, found no due process violation.


OUTCOME: Appellate court judgment reversed; constitutional guarantee of jury trial was not intended to guarantee jury trial for uninsured-motorist coverage, and remedy did not exist at common law but instead was devised by legislature.

Ill. Republican Party v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections


Docket No. 85176


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


188 Ill. 2d 70; 720 N.E.2d 231; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 976; 241 Ill. Dec. 776



October 21, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court, Fourth District. CASE NUMBERS: AC4-97-0183, AC4-97-0184, SBE97CD1, SBE97CD2.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part; Board decision set aside; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents petitioned for leave to appeal an order from the Appellate Court (Illinois), which, upon complainant's appeal from an order of the election board, remanded the cause to the board, ordering that those members who voted that the complaints were not filed on justifiable grounds state a record of their reasons.


OVERVIEW: Complainant appealed an order of the board of elections (board) directly to the appellate court, as provided by section 9-22 of the election code (10 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-22 (West 1996)). The appellate court remanded the cause to the board, ordering that those members who voted that the complaints were not filed on justifiable grounds state their reasons for so voting. Respondents petitioned the court for leave to appeal, and the court granted the motion. The court found that at the conclusion of the preliminary hearing, the board failed to achieve a vote of five members to dismiss the complaints as not filed on justifiable grounds. They noted that the board may not dismiss a complaint after the closed preliminary hearing unless at least five members vote to do so. Thus, the court held that the complaints were then required to proceed to a public hearing.


OUTCOME: Judgment remanding the proceeding to the board was affirmed, but the remainder of the opinion was vacated, because after the closed preliminary hearing less than five members of the election board voted to dismiss the complaint, the complaints were required to proceed to a public hearing.

 

10 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Turner


Docket No. 79902


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


187 Ill. 2d 406; 719 N.E.2d 725; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 959; 241 Ill. Dec. 596



September 23, 1999, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from Macoupin County Circuit Court (Illinois) order granting prosecution's motion to dismiss the post-conviction petition without an evidentiary hearing, holding the claims in the post-conviction petition were barred by res judicata or waived because petitioner could have raised the claims on direct appeal but failed to do so.


OVERVIEW: In a criminal case involving murder and aggravated kidnapping charges, petitioner was sentenced to death. Petitioner appealed from an order granting the prosecution's motion to dismiss his post-conviction petition without an evidentiary hearing, holding that the claims in the post-conviction petition were barred by the doctrine of res judicata or waived because the petitioner could have raised the claims on direct appeal but failed to do so. The appellate court reversed and remanded. The court considered the totality of the circumstances and held that post-conviction counsel's performance was unreasonable and fell below the level of assistance required by Ill. S. Ct. R. 651(c). Counsel failed to make a routine amendment to the post-conviction petition which would have overcome the procedural bar of waiver and elected to stand on the pro se petition, omitting the essential elements of the petitioner's constitutional claims and contained virtually no evidentiary support.


OUTCOME: Court reversed and remanded, because post-conviction counsel's performance was unreasonable and below required level of assistance. Counsel failed to make routine amendment to post-conviction petition which would have overcome procedural bar of waiver and elected to stand on pro se petition, omitting essential elements of constitutional claims.

 

11 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Morgan


Docket No. 82374


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


187 Ill. 2d 500; 719 N.E.2d 681; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 960; 241 Ill. Dec. 552



September 23, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1982.
Writ of certiorari denied Morgan v. Illinois, 529 U.S. 1023, 120 S. Ct. 1429, 146 L. Ed. 2d 320, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1982 (2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Morgan, 212 Ill. 2d 148, 817 N.E.2d 524, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1021, 288 Ill. Dec. 166 (2004)
Appeal after remand at People v. Morgan, 375 Ill. App. 3d 525, 875 N.E.2d 6, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 898, 314 Ill. Dec. 627 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Morgan, 112 Ill. 2d 111, 492 N.E.2d 1303, 1986 Ill. LEXIS 245, 97 Ill. Dec. 430 (1986)



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned pursuant to the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. (West 1994), challenging his convictions and the circuit court's imposition of a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court found defendant eligible for the death penalty on the basis that he was convicted of murdering two individuals. Defendant failed to make a substantial showing of a violation of his right to effective assistance of counsel at the guilt-innocence phase of trial and at death penalty eligibility. However, trial counsel was ineffective at the sentencing phase of his trial because counsel failed to investigate and present mitigating evidence of defendant's organic brain damage. The court held that the post-conviction judge's finding that defense counsel satisfied the performance prong of the Strickland test was manifestly erroneous. Failure to investigate and present mitigating evidence constituted representation that fell below objective standards of reasonableness under prevailing professional norms. Therefore, defendant satisfied the first prong of Strickland. The second prong was satisfied because counsel's deficient performance so prejudiced defendant that he was denied a fair sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: Convictions affirmed because right to effective assistance of counsel at the guilt-innocence phase of trial and at death penalty eligibility not violated. Death sentence vacated and cause remanded because defense counsel's failure to present and investigate mitigating evidence so prejudiced the defendant that his sentencing hearing was fundamentally unfair.

 

12 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fuller


Docket No. 86104


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


187 Ill. 2d 1; 714 N.E.2d 501; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 952; 239 Ill. Dec. 582



July 1, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court, Kane County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. John L. Petersen. CASE NUMBERS: TR97CF1248.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prosecutor appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kane County (Illinois) that found the penalty imposed against defendant for violation of 625 ILCS 5/4-103(a)(6) was unconstitutional as it was applied to her under the facts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant falsely reported to police that her ex-husband had stolen her car. She was charged with filing a false report of vehicle theft in violation of 625 ILCS 5/4-103(a)(6), which was a Class 2 felony. Defendant moved to dismiss the charge on the ground that the punishment was disproportionate to the crime. The trial court agreed that the punishment was unconstitutional as applied to defendant, and the prosecutor appealed. The court reversed and remanded. Under the proportionate penalty clause of the Illinois Constitution, review was available only if the punishment was cruel, degrading, or wholly disproportionate, if when comparing similar offenses the punishment was apparently disproportionate, or if identical offenses were given different sentences. Defendant was not entitled to relief under the first form of review because causing an innocent person to be charged with a crime was a serious offense, and the punishment for this offense as a felony was not disproportionate. Under the second form of review, the punishment was also valid because the punishment was appropriate for preventing fraudulent conduct involving vehicles.


OUTCOME: Judgment dismissing charge against defendant for filing false report of car theft was reversed and remanded because Class 2 felony sentence was not disproportionate to the crime.

 

13 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. K.C. (In re K.C.)


Docket Nos. 86364, 86365 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


186 Ill. 2d 542; 714 N.E.2d 491; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 957; 239 Ill. Dec. 572



July 1, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court, Cook County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Martin Agran, CASE NUMBERS: TR98JD6669.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Cook County (Illinois), which granted respondent juveniles' motion to strike amendments to the petition for adjudication of wardship, which had alleged violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/4-102(a), on the ground that the statute violated state and federal due process provisions by potentially punishing wholly innocent conduct without requiring a culpable mental state.


OVERVIEW: As a threshold matter, the appellate court held that the trial court correctly concluded that 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/4-102(a) imposed absolute liability, noting that the legislature's intent to impose absolute liability was supported by the specific deletion of mental states from 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/4-102(a)'s unambiguous provisions as well as the statute's legislative history. The appellate court then agreed that that the challenged sections under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/4-102(a) violated the due process clauses of the federal and state constitutions. The appellate court noted that the operation of the statute potentially to punish wholly innocent conduct without requiring a culpable mental state conflicted with the legislature's goal of protecting otherwise innocent conduct from criminal prosecution. The appellate court affirmed, finding that the motion to strike was properly granted where the statutory provisions in question swept too broadly and attempted to punish persons with wholly innocent motives.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting respondent juveniles' motion to strike amendments to appellant state's petition for adjudication of wardship where the statutory sections in question, which imposed absolute liability for damaging a motor vehicle, violated federal and state due process clauses by potentially punishing wholly innocent conduct without requiring a culpable mental state.

 

14 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Arangold Corp. v. Zehnder


Docket No. 85366


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


187 Ill. 2d 341; 718 N.E.2d 191; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 955; 240 Ill. Dec. 710



July 1, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court for Cook County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. John A. Ward. CASE NUMBERS: TR95L50989.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Director of Revenue, the State Treasurer, and the Department of Revenue, appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Cook County (Illinois) holding that Public Act 89-21 was invalid in its entirety for violating the single subject rule and entering a final judgment for plaintiff in its action to enjoin the enforcement of a tobacco tax enacted as part of Public Act 89-21 and to recover monies paid under protest toward the tax.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff corporation brought this action to enjoin the enforcement of a tobacco tax that was enacted as part of Public Act 89-21 (Act) and to recover those monies that it had paid under protest toward the tax. The circuit court held that the Act was unconstitutional in its entirety because it violated the single subject requirement of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) (1970). Defendants, the Director of Revenue, the State Treasurer, and the Department of Revenue, appealed. The court held that the Act embraced but a single subject, the implementation of the state budget for the 1996 fiscal year. The original bill introduced in the Senate, the subsequent conference committee report, and the final enactment of the Act all pertained to this subject. Although Public Act 89-21 had a number of provisions and amended a number of acts already then in effect, every provision within the Act was germane to this single subject. Therefore, all matters included within the Act had a natural and logical connection to implementation of the state's budget for the 1996 fiscal year. The Act thus comported with the single subject rule. Therefore, the court reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision below that found that the act in question violated the single subject rule and was unconstitutional. The court remanded the case and concluded that the act embraced the single subject of implementation, the state budget for the 1996 fiscal year.

 

15 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Heard


Docket No. 81443


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


187 Ill. 2d 36; 718 N.E.2d 58; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 677; 240 Ill. Dec. 577



June 17, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 6, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1751. As Amended September 30, 1999.
Writ of certiorari denied Heard v. Illinois, 529 U.S. 1004, 120 S. Ct. 1268, 146 L. Ed. 2d 218, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1751 (2000)
Related proceeding at People ex rel. Madigan v. Snyder, 208 Ill. 2d 457, 804 N.E.2d 546, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 6, 281 Ill. Dec. 581 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Case Number: TR94CR04637.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment convicting defendant of three counts of first degree murder, denied defendant's motion for a new trial or for acquittal, and which found defendant eligible for the death penalty pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(b)(3) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff State of Illinois brought charges against defendant, contending he killed his ex-girlfriend, her new boyfriend, and her sister. The ex-girlfriend's daughter, who was present at the time of the murders, testified that defendant shot and killed the victims. Defendant was convicted of the murders and was sentenced to death pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(b)(3) (1992). Defendant contended, among other things, that the trial court improperly admitted prejudicial evidence, that the prosecutor engaged in discriminatory jury selection, that his trial counsel was ineffective, and that the death sentence was improperly imposed. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions and his sentence. The appellate court found that evidence of other crimes was admissible to show intent to commit the murders, that defendant failed to establish a prima facie case of jury discrimination in the jury selection, and that defense counsel's strategic moves could not be considered ineffective assistance. Finally, the court found that the death sentence was appropriate because the murders were the culmination of an escalating history of violence by defendant against the victims.


OUTCOME: Decision of the lower court convicting defendant of three counts of first degree murder, denying defendant's motion for a new trial, and sentencing defendant to death was affirmed. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdicts against defendant and that defendant's evidentiary challenges and claims of ineffective assistance of counsel did not rise to the level of reversible error.

 

16 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brooks


Docket No. 81624


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


187 Ill. 2d 91; 718 N.E.2d 88; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 678; 240 Ill. Dec. 607



June 17, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, 10/04/1999
Writ of certiorari denied Brooks v. Illinois, 529 U.S. 1039, 120 S. Ct. 1534, 146 L. Ed. 2d 349, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2236 (2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Brooks, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2772, 2012 IL App (1st) 090104-U (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Trial Judge: Hon. Earl E. Strayhorn. Case Number: TR91CR21147.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment convicting defendant of six counts of first degree murder and three counts of attempted first degree murder and sentenced him to death. Plaintiff State of Illinois alleged defendant shot the victims during an altercation with a rival gang.


OVERVIEW: Defendant gang member was arrested as the alleged trigger man in a drive-by shooting. Plaintiff State of Illinois charged defendant and several others with murders. Following a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of six counts of murder in the first degree and three counts of attempted murder and was sentenced to death. Defendant's conviction was based primarily upon statements given by eyewitnesses. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to convict him, that some of the identifications were inadmissible, that his counsel was ineffective, and that his sentence was improper. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and the sentence. The appellate court reasoned that once witness statements were determined to be admissible, its standard of review was limited to determining whether, viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the State, any rational trier of fact could have found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court found that the verdict was supported by the evidence and that the sentence was properly imposed.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court convicting defendant of murder and attempted murder and sentencing him to death was affirmed. The court found that even though defendant met his burden of showing that an identification was impermissibly suggestive, plaintiff state showed the identification was based on independent recollection. The court also found that the sentence was appropriate because of the lack of mitigating circumstances.

 

17 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nielson


Docket No. 83127


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


187 Ill. 2d 271; 718 N.E.2d 131; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 680; 240 Ill. Dec. 650



June 17, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied April 24, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2908.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wayne County. Trial Judge: Hon. Loren P. Lewis. Case Number: TR95CF76.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of Wayne County (Illinois), of two counts of first degree murder and two counts of concealing a homicidal death. The same jury sentenced him to death for the murders, and the trial court imposed two extended 10-year sentences for the concealment convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of two counts of first degree murder in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a) (1), (a)(2) (1996) and two counts of concealing a homicidal death in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-3.1(a) (1996) after he shot, dismembered, and burned his victims. Defendant appealed and argued, inter alia, that the trial court violated his constitutional rights by conducting the sentencing phase outside his presence, that it improperly admitted evidence that was irrelevant and prejudicial, that it erred in imposing extended sentences for the concealment convictions, and that the death penalty was unconstitutional. The court ruled that the extended sentences were improper because defendant dismembered the victims after they were dead, and one could not inflict pain and suffering on a dead body. Otherwise, the court affirmed the convictions and sentences as imposed. The court noted that defendant clearly waived his right to be present at the sentencing phase of the trial and that the rules of evidence at trial did not apply to the sentencing phase so that the trial court could learn of both aggravating and mitigating circumstances before imposing sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the imposition of the death penalty upon defendant for the first-degree murder convictions, but the court modified the extended sentences imposed for the concealment convictions because defendant dismembered the victims after he had already killed them.

 

18 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lantz


Docket Nos. 83527, 83641 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


186 Ill. 2d 243; 712 N.E.2d 314; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 667; 238 Ill. Dec. 592



April 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 83527 - Appeal from the Appellate Court, Second District of Lake County. Trial Judge: Hon. Raymond J. McKoski. Case Numbers: AC2-95-1569, TR95CF644.

No. 83641 - Appeal from the Appellate Court, Second District of DuPage County. Trial Judge: Hon. John J. Nelligan. Case Numbers: AC2-95-0527, TR93CH805.



DISPOSITION: No. 83527-Judgment affirmed. No. 83641-Judgment reversed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Consolidated appeals from a decision of the Appellate Courts, Second District of Lake County and DuPage County (Illinois), finding the Illinois Guilty but Mentally Ill Statute, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-4(j) (1994), unconstitutional and reversing the convictions of two criminal defendants convicted of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The first degree murder convictions of two criminal defendants were overturned following the appellate courts' determination that the Illinois Guilty but Mentally Ill Statute, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-4(j) (1994), was unconstitutional. The supreme court rejected the argument that the statutory scheme was confusing and violated due process because it encouraged juries to reach compromise verdicts, and that the statute placed conflicting burdens on the defense by requiring the defense to prove both insanity and mental illness. The court here found that the sequence in which the juries resolved those issues demonstrated that the defense in guilty but mentally ill cases did not have the burden of establishing conflicting propositions at the same time. In upholding the constitutionality of the guilty but mentally ill statute, the court further determined that the statute did not encourage the juries to render false compromise verdicts.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the constitutionality of Illinois' guilty but mentally ill statute. The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court regarding first defendant's conviction, and reversed in part, vacated in part and remanded the second defendant's case to the appellate court for further proceedings.

People v. Buss


Docket No. 81911


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


187 Ill. 2d 144; 718 N.E.2d 1; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 663; 240 Ill. Dec. 520

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal, Circuit Court, Will County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Gerald R. Kinney, CASE NUMBERS: TR95CF5046.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court, Will County (Illinois), which found him guilty of first degree murder, aggravated kidnapping, aggravated unlawful restraint, and imposed upon him the death penalty, claiming errors relating to voir dire, the denial of his pretrial motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence, errors that occurred at trial, and errors at both stages of the sentencing hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was spotted by eyewitnesses being near and around the victim, a 10-year old boy, who disappeared shortly thereafter. The court also concluded that the jury properly considered defendant's aggravating and mitigation factors, before sentencing him to death, and that the state's death penalty statute was constitutional.

Gebis v. Swietek (In re Estate of Gebis)


Docket No. 85909


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


186 Ill. 2d 188; 710 N.E.2d 385; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 25; 237 Ill. Dec. 755



March 18, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court, Cook County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Maureen E. Connors. CASE NUMBERS: TR94P6222.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), which declared 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-1.1 unconstitutional and in doing so, denied his claim against the guardianship estate of his ward for compensation for caring for the ward during the final years of her life.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and appellee were guardians of their late mother and her estate. Four months after the ward died, appellant presented a statutory custodial claim, pursuant to 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-1.1, against the guardianship for $ 361,320 in compensation for caring for the ward during her lifetime. Appellee filed a motion to dismiss the claim and asserted, among other things, that the statute was unconstitutional, and requested dismissal of the claim. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss the claim and held that the statute violated substantive due process, the equal protection clause, and it constituted special legislation. On appeal, the court vacated the judgment of the trial court and held that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to adjudicate the constitutionality of a statutory custodial claim filed against the ward's guardianship estate because the guardianship ceased at the ward's death and that appellant's claim for custodial care could only be properly filed against the decedent's estate.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment finding the statutory custodial claim statute unconstitutional and held that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to determine any claim against the guardianship estate after the ward died because the ward then became a decedent, and claims could then only be made against the decedent's estate. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

21 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carlson


Docket No. 83093


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


185 Ill. 2d 546; 708 N.E.2d 372; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 19; 236 Ill. Dec. 786



February 19, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, Second District. Kane County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Barry E. Puklin. CASE NUMBERS: AC2-96-0307, TR94CF1188.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court, Second Circuit, Kane County (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's suppression order, finding that the evidence seized was admissible pursuant to the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule.


OVERVIEW: A United States postal inspector searched an express mail package addressed to defendant pursuant to a federal search warrant after a narcotics-trained police dog had alerted to it. The package contained a controlled substance. The postal inspector resealed the package and contacted state police who requested an anticipatory search warrant to be executed only upon the conditions that a postal inspector, posing as a postal carrier, deliver the package to defendant's address and that an occupant of the residence accept the package. The warrant was executed and police recovered the controlled substance. At trial, defendant filed a motion to quash the search warrant and suppress the evidence. The circuit court initially denied defendant's motion. However, after an opinion holding that anticipatory search warrants were not authorized by statute and were therefore invalid, the circuit court suppressed the evidence. The prosecution appealed and the appellate court reversed the suppression order. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, finding that the evidence seized was admissible pursuant to the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which reversed the suppression order. The court held that the evidence was admissible under the good-faith exception. The court held that anticipatory search warrants did not suffer from a probable cause defect, thus, anticipatory search warrants did not violate either the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution or the search and seizure clause of the Illinois Constitution.

DeLuna v. Treister


Docket Nos. 83119, 83171 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


185 Ill. 2d 565; 708 N.E.2d 340; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 16; 236 Ill. Dec. 754



February 19, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, First District. Cook County. CASE NUMBERS: AC1-94-1397, AC1-94-2719, TR93L13826.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a hospital and the decedent's physician, filed a petition for leave to appeal from a decision of the Appellate Court, First District, Cook County (Illinois), which reversed a trial court decision dismissing a suit by plaintiff estate administrator against defendants for determination of whether an involuntary dismissal for not complying with 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-622 constituted an adjudication on the merits.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff estate administrator filed a medical malpractice action against defendants, the decedent's treating physician and a hospital that employed the physician, contending that defendant physician negligently caused decedent's death and defendant hospital was vicariously liable. The trial court granted a dismissal motion by defendant physician and also dismissed the action against defendant hospital under respondeat superior principles. Plaintiff successfully appealed where the appeals court reversed the trial court judgment in a split decision. Defendants then filed petitions for leave to appeal, which were granted by the state supreme court. The court applied 134 Ill. 2d R. 273, which stated that an order of dismissal was an involuntary dismissal unless for lack of jurisdiction, improper venue, or failure to join an indispensable party, and was an adjudication on the merits. The court reversed the decision of the trial court as to the dismissal of defendant hospital but affirmed the trial court dismissal as to defendant physician because the action was not time-barred against the hospital. The case was remanded back to the trial court for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial and appeals court judgments and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. The court reversed the decision of the trial court dismissing defendant hospital because an action against it was not time-barred, but affirmed dismissal as to defendant physician because his dismissal was on the merits under state procedural rules and was res judicata in any subsequent actions.

Hearne v. Illinois State Bd. of Educ.


Docket Nos. 84242, 84311 cons.

DISPOSITION: Cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) holding that § 34-85 of the School Code, 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/34-85 (1996), unconstitutionally violated the due process rights of tenured teachers.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was employed by defendant school board and was a tenured teacher. Defendant's general superintendent charged plaintiff with conduct unbecoming a teacher and gross dereliction of duties. The hearing officer issued written findings of fact, concluding that defendant failed to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that plaintiff was guilty of the three charges alleged. A decision that § 34-85 of the School Code, 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/34-85 (1996), unconstitutionally violated the due process rights of tenured teachers was remanded. People v. Reedy


Docket Nos. 85191, 85297 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


186 Ill. 2d 1; 708 N.E.2d 1114; 1999 Ill. LEXIS 1; 237 Ill. Dec. 74



January 22, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 30, 1999.



DISPOSITION: No. 85191-Appellate court judgment affirmed. No. 85297-Appellate court judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants challenged judgments from the Circuit Courts, Lake County and Peoria County (Illinois) respectively, in a consolidated appeal, after both were sentenced, following felony convictions, under the truth-in-sentencing law, which was part of Ill. Pub. Act 89-404.


OVERVIEW: Two defendants were convicted of separate offenses, but were both sentenced pursuant to the Illinois truth-in-sentencing law contained in Ill. Pub. Act 89-404. Regarding the first defendant, an appellate court held that the Act violated the single subject clause of the Illinois Constitution, held the Act void in its entirety, and enjoined the state from enforcing the Act. The state then appealed to the supreme court. Regarding the other defendant, an appellate court ruled that he had no standing on direct appeal to challenge the constitutionality of the Act, and the state supreme court granted his petition to appeal. In the consolidated appeal, the supreme court affirmed the appellate court regarding the first defendant, reversed the appellate court regarding the other defendant, and ruled that the general assembly violated the single subject clause of Ill. Const. 1970, art. IV, § 8(d) when it enacted the law, which was thereby ruled unconstitutional. The court further held that although Ill. Pub. Act 90-592 recodified the truth-in-sentencing legislation in its entirety, the curative function could only be applied prospectively, and, therefore, did not apply to these cases.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment the court of appeals, regarding one defendant, and reversed the judgment of the court of appeals, regarding the other defendant, holding that the Illinois truth-in-sentencing law, under which both were sentenced, was unconstitutional because it was part of an act which violated the single-subject clause of the Illinois Constitution.

People v. Terrell


Docket No. 79312


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 7, 1999. Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5948.
Rehearing denied by People v. Terrell, 1999 Ill. LEXIS 640 (Ill., Mar. 29, 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Terrell v. Illinois, 528 U.S. 881, 120 S. Ct. 194, 145 L. Ed. 2d 163, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5948 (1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Terrell, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1279 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal, Circuit Court, Cook County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Christy S. Berkos. CASE NUMBERS: TR85CR10757.
Terrell v. Illinois, 493 U.S. 959, 495 U.S. 959, 110 S. Ct. 2567, 109 L. Ed. 2d 749, 1990 U.S. LEXIS 2745 (1990)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of the sexual assault and murder of a 15-month old girl. He was sentenced to death for the murder and to 60 years for the sexual assault. On a previous appeal the court affirmed the conviction but vacated the sentence and remanded for a new sentencing hearing. At the resentencing defendant was again sentenced to death. The death sentence was stayed pending direct appeal by defendant to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised 24 separate issues as grounds to vacate his death sentence. The court affirmed the death sentence, holding that defendant's proposed question during jury selection was not compelled. To be constitutionally compelled, it was not enough that a voir dire question be helpful, rather, the trial court's failure to ask the question had to render the proceedings fundamentally unfair. The court found that although the trial court should not have made some of the comments that it did, none of the comments were so prejudicial as to damage the impartiality of the jury. The court held that the State properly relied on Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(7), (6)(c) (1985) as aggravating factors during the eligibility stage of sentencing. The court held that at the aggravation-mitigation stage of sentencing the only requirement for admissibility was that the evidence be relevant and reliable. The court held defendant failed to timely raise objections to the evidence. The court held that the jury instructions were constitutional under the applicable standard. The court held that a death sentence would not be overturned lightly, and that defendant's was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence of death.

People v. Davis


Docket No. 81595


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


185 Ill. 2d 317; 706 N.E.2d 473; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1920; 235 Ill. Dec. 918



December 31, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court, Henry County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Jeffrey W. O'Connor. CASE NUMBERS: TR95CF275, TR96CF100.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was charged first degree murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, aggravated kidnapping, and concealment of a homicidal death. The Circuit Court, Henry County (Illinois) convicted him and assessed the death penalty. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted for the crimes of first-degree murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, aggravated kidnapping, and concealment of a homicidal death. The jury found defendant eligible for the death penalty under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(b)(6) (1994). The defendant waived his right to a jury for the second phase of the sentencing hearing and the trial court sentenced him on death. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the denial of an opportunity to cross-examine a witness about the nature of his pending felony charge in another state was harmless where the evidence of the defendant's guilt was overwhelming, (2) the deficiency prong of the ineffective assistance of counsel test need not be considered where the defendant fails to show how he was prejudiced by counsels acts or omissions, (3) evidence of the defendant's adjustment to incarceration was relevant on the issue of mitigation in connection with the death penalty, (4) Illinois death penalty statute was constitutional, and (6) the conviction was proper but the trial court's refusal to consider the mitigating evidence was error that required that the death penalty sentence be vacated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's convictions but his death sentence vacated and the cause remanded because the trial court had impermissibly refused to consider evidence of the defendant's adjustment to incarceration as a mitigating factor when it assessed the death penalty.

City of Chicago v. Roman


Docket No. 84268


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 504; 705 N.E.2d 81; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1913; 235 Ill. Dec. 468



December 17, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, First District. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. William P. O'Malley. CASE NUMBERS: AC1-96-1957, TR94MC1351250.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Appellate Court, First Division (Illinois) reversing defendant's sentence that was less than the mandatory minimum sentence prescribed by Chicago, Ill. Mun. Code § 8-4-080.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of assault against the elderly in violation of § 8-4-080. The trial court ruled that the mandatory minimum sentence that the ordinance prescribed, imprisonment for 90 days, exceeded the city's home rule authority. Thus, the trial court sentenced defendant to 10 days of community service and to one year of probation. City appealed. The appellate court concluded that it was within city's constitutional powers as a home rule unit to have a sentencing scheme different from that of the state, and state law did not prevent or restrict the city from prescribing mandatory imprisonment as a penalty in the ordinance. On appeal from defendant's resentencing consistent with § 8-4-080, the court held that the Unified Code of Corrections did not partially preempt § 8-4-080 or require that the ordinance conform to the Code. The court found that since city had the home rule authority to establish a 90-day mandatory minimum sentence, and because the General Assembly had not specifically preempted or limited that authority, the prescribed penalty in § 8-4-080 constituted a valid exercise of city's home rule power.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

28 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lombardi


Docket Nos. 83810, 83950, 83951, 83952 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 462; 705 N.E.2d 91; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1918; 235 Ill. Dec. 478



December 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court. Kankakee County. CASE NUMBERS: TR95CF678, TR96CF695, TR96CF696, TR97CF214. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Daniel W. Gould.



DISPOSITION: Nos. 83810 & 83952-Reversed and remanded. Nos. 83950 & 83951-Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Illinois appealed orders of the Kankakee County Circuit Court (Illinois), which dismissed the armed violence charges against four defendants on the basis that the penalty for armed violence violated the due process and proportionate penalties provisions of Ill. Const. 1970, art. I, §§ 2, 11.


OVERVIEW: Two defendants were charged with armed violence under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33A-1 et seq. (West 1996), based on possession of a controlled substance while armed with a gun, and two were charged with armed violence predicated on residential burglary while armed with a gun, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33A-2 (West 1996). The trial court dismissed the charges as in violation of the due process and proportionality provisions of the Illinois Constitution, and the State appealed. The court held that there was no due process violation because the legislature could reasonably have found that the statute was necessary to achieve the goal of discouraging offenders from carrying a weapon during a felony. The statute also did not violate the proportionate penalties clause even though it did not vary with the seriousness of the underlying crime because the legislature was allowed to focus on the use of the weapon. However, with respect to the burglary defendants, the armed violence statute violated the proportionate penalties clause because it imposed a more severe penalty than that imposed for the offense of home invasion, which was a more serious crime than burglary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the armed violence charges against the burglary defendants, but reversed the dismissal of the armed violence charges against the controlled substance defendants.

People v. Fisher


Docket Nos. 82308, 82309, 82310, 82311 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 441; 705 N.E.2d 67; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1915; 235 Ill. Dec. 454



December 17, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant vehicle drivers each filed a petition to rescind the summary suspension of their driving privileges. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) stayed its order rescinding the vehicle drivers' suspensions pending appeal by the State.


OVERVIEW: The vehicle drivers maintained that their license suspensions were unconstitutional on both equal protection and due process grounds. The court held that when viewed as a means of providing motivation for non-first offenders to submit to testing to determine blood-alcohol content, the distinction which 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-208.1(g) (1996) drew between those drivers who submitted to chemical testing and those drivers who refused was neither irrational nor arbitrary. The court noted that the vehicle drivers had cited no authority in support of their argument that the right to equal protection of the laws was violated by eliminating hardship relief for drivers who refused to submit to chemical testing but not for those who failed such testing. The court stated that the two-year suspension with no hardship relief provided arrested drivers with an incentive to submit to testing for blood-alcohol content and, therefore, was rationally related to the legitimate state goal of promoting highway safety. Accordingly, the court concluded that 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-208.1(a)(3), (g) (1996) did not violate the vehicle drivers' substantive due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the cause for further proceedings consistent with the opinion of the court.

People v. Placek


Docket No. 84685


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 370; 704 N.E.2d 393; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1589; 235 Ill. Dec. 44



December 3, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court, First District of Cook County. Nos. AC1-95-4398, TR93CR19851. Honorable Joseph J. Urso.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of theft, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16-1(a)(5) (1989), and delivery of a controlled substance and possession with intent to deliver, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(a)(2). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted defendant's motion for a new trial and dismissed the theft charge. Defendant appealed the affirmance of his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the State's improper introduction of other-crimes evidence at defendant's second trial constituted reversible error. The State improperly introduced other-crimes evidence in defendant's second trial, and the introduction of the evidence warranted reversal and remanded for a new trial. The circuit court abused its discretion in allowing the admission of evidence that defendant dealt in stolen auto parts. This evidence was not admissible under the entrapment exception to the general rule prohibiting other-crimes evidence because it was not specifically relevant to the crimes for which defendant claimed he was entrapped. The testimony that defendant dealt in stolen auto parts was not relevant to either the crimes with which defendant was charged or defendant's predisposition to commit those crimes. Defendant was charged with delivery of a controlled substance and possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, not auto parts theft. Theft of auto parts was not similar to the crime of delivery of cocaine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the cause to the circuit court for a new trial.

People v. Kliner


Docket No. 81314


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


185 Ill. 2d 81; 705 N.E.2d 850; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1582; 235 Ill. Dec. 667



December 3, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5195.
Rehearing denied by People v. Kliner, 1999 Ill. LEXIS 652 (Ill., Feb. 1, 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Kliner v. Illinois, 528 U.S. 831, 120 S. Ct. 86, 145 L. Ed. 2d 73, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5195 (1999)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Dismissed by People v. Kliner, 203 Ill. 2d 402, 786 N.E.2d 976, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1641, 272 Ill. Dec. 142 (2002)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Kliner v. McCann, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 94443 (N.D. Ill., Nov. 13, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Motion denied by People v. Kliner, 2013 IL App (1st) 110785-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1430 (2013)
Decision reached on appeal by People v. Kliner, 2014 IL App (1st) 122285-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2676 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. TR93CR1547620. Honorable Janice Bierman, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of first degree murder. He was found eligible for the death penalty on the basis that he committed the murder under an agreement for which he was to receive money. Ill. Rev. Stat. 1987, ch. 38, par. 9-1(b)(5). He was sentenced to death and his sentence was stayed pending review by the court pursuant to Ill. Const. 1970, art. VI, § 4(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and co-defendant were hired by the victim's husband to kill her in exchange for money. Defendant shot the victim five times. On review, the court found that: (1) defendant was brought to trial within the time limits of the speedy trial statute, Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-3-5 (1994); (2) although the State's remarks in its opening statements about defendant's possession and purchase of handguns were improper, they did not create reversible error; (3) any errors in limiting defendant's cross-examination of his ex-girlfriend or the victim's husband were harmless beyond a reasonable doubt; (4) co-defendant's statements were admissible under the co-conspirator exception to the hearsay rule; (5) the State's comments during closing arguments did not operate to deny defendant of a fair trial or due process of law; (6) the judge's ex parte communications with the jury were harmless beyond a reasonable doubt; (7) defendant was not denied a fair sentencing hearing; and (8) a more severe sentence for defendant was justified and proper given the circumstances of the murder, his character, and his background.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and affirmed his death sentence.

People v. Every


Docket No. 84909


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 281; 703 N.E.2d 897; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1580; 234 Ill. Dec. 797



November 19, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. JoDaviess County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Victor V. Sprengelmeyer. CASE NUMBERS: TR97DT40.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court in JoDaviess County (Illinois), which determined that 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.1(a) (1996) was unconstitutional and suppressed the evidence of defendant's blood-alcohol level based on a sample taken in an Iowa hospital.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a one-car accident and was transported for medical treatment to a hospital in another state. Defendant was issued a citation for driving while intoxicated, pursuant to Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501(a)(2) (1996), and the officer had a blood sample taken at the hospital. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence of his blood-alcohol level and contended that Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.1(a) (1996) was unconstitutional because it allowed officers to obtain blood samples from other states for incidents that occurred in Illinois. The court determined that, while the officer had no more authority than a private citizen did when outside his jurisdiction, the officer was operating as an agent for the state. The officer was not precluded from obtaining evidence outside of his jurisdiction. The court determined that § 11-501.1(a), the implied consent statute, authorized the officer to collect blood samples from other states. The court held that defendant had impliedly consented to the procedure in § 11-501.1(a) and he should not be relieved of the consequences simply because he was transported to another state for treatment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the suppression of the evidence of defendant's blood-alcohol level and the determination that portions of the implied consent statute were unconstitutional. The case was remanded to the trial court.

People v. Bull

Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Brown, 2013 IL App (1st) 091009, 988 N.E.2d 1063, 2013 Ill. App. LEXIS 237, 370 Ill. Dec. 707 (2013)

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. TR94CR4431. Honorable Vincent M. Gaughan, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, which convicted him on two counts of first degree murder and on one count each of aggravated vehicular hijacking, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and armed robbery. Defendant was sentenced to death for the convictions for first-degree murder, but his execution was stayed pending his appeal.

Defendant next argued that the prosecutor, in his opening statement, improperly alluded to inadmissible victim impact evidence and that the allusion to the lives of the victims was improper. The court held that because the defense counsel did not object to that portion of the prosecutor's opening statement, defendant's belated objection was considered waived. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that if any error occurred during trial, it was slight and did not rise to the level of plain error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and entered an order setting the date on which the sentence of death was to be carried out.

People v. Hope


Docket No. 80753


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 39; 702 N.E.2d 1282; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1574; 234 Ill. Dec. 379



October 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. TR82C1179. Honorable Thomas R. Fitzgerald, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant made a direct appeal of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment convicting him of murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a black man, pleaded guilty to killing a white police officer and attempting to kill a second officer. A jury found two aggravating factors and no mitigating factors and sentenced defendant to death. On appeal was the issue of the trial court's refusal to question the jury venire on the issue of interracial crime bias even after defense counsel requested such a question. The court held that the trial court's refusal to question the jury venire on the issue was an abuse of discretion. At the time of defendant's sentencing, both the court and the United States Supreme Court had determined that such an inquiry was constitutionally mandated when requested under circumstances such as defendant's. The trial court was bound to follow precedent. The court then held that on remand, victim impact statements from family of the current victims were appropriate but statements by victims of defendant's previous crimes would not be admissible. While evidence of defendant's prior crimes, including a prior murder, was relevant to aggravation because it illuminated the character and record of defendant, the unforeseen effects of those prior crimes on others was of no such value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder and attempted murder convictions but vacated his death sentence and remanded for resentencing.

People v. Macri


Docket No. 80107


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


185 Ill. 2d 1; 705 N.E.2d 772; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1576; 235 Ill. Dec. 589



October 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5172.
Rehearing denied by People v. Macri, 1999 Ill. LEXIS 651 (Ill., Feb. 1, 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Macri v. Illinois, 528 U.S. 829, 120 S. Ct. 83, 145 L. Ed. 2d 70, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5172 (1999)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Dismissed by People v. Macri, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1265 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, DuPage County. No. TR93CF1879. Honorable Ann B. Jorgensen, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court, DuPage County (Illinois), which sentenced him to death after he was convicted of intentional murder pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1), knowing murder pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(2), felony murder pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(3), and aggravated criminal sexual assault pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-14(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his death sentence was improper on various grounds. The court held that defendant was not entitled to a new sentencing hearing. The court found that the record showed that the jurors were appropriately instructed at both the eligibility phase and the aggravation-mitigation phase of the sentencing hearing concerning the unanimity requirement. The court held that defendant was not deprived of a fair death sentence eligibility hearing even though the prosecutor remarked that by killing his victim, he eliminated a witness in a rape case. The court found that the remark did not allow the jury to consider a legally unavailable aggravating circumstance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that defendant's various contentions were without merit and that his death sentence was proper.

People v. Koppa


Docket No. 83962


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 159; 703 N.E.2d 91; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1564; 234 Ill. Dec. 479



October 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. TR96CR25179. Honorable Michael J. Pope, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed two counts of armed violence from the defendant's indictment, which also included counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and aggravated kidnapping, based on the finding that the armed violence counts violated the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, and improperly constituted double enhancement because the weapon factor was used twice. The State sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the State properly charged defendant with separate counts for each aggravating factor because the armed violence charges were not identical to the aggravated criminal sexual abuse or aggravated kidnapping charges. The elements of armed violence based on the predicate felony of aggravated criminal sexual abuse were the commission of criminal sexual abuse, presence of a weapon, and bodily harm to the victim, while aggravated criminal sexual abuse based on bodily harm did not have the presence of a weapon. The armed violence charge based on aggravated kidnapping involved the commission of kidnapping while armed with a dangerous weapon and concealing identity, while aggravated kidnapping involved kidnapping and a weapon, but not concealment of identity. Because the armed violence statute properly penalized the entirety of defendant's alleged conduct, the greater penalty provided for did not violate the proportionality clause. Double enhancement did not occur because the State did not use a weapon factor or bodily harm factor twice to enhance the predicate felonies of criminal sexual abuse or kidnapping to aggravating offenses and then the armed violence charges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal and reinstated the counts of armed violence, remanding for further proceedings.

 

38 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Barbara H. (In re Barbara H.)


Docket Nos. 83418, 83486 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


183 Ill. 2d 482; 702 N.E.2d 555; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1566; 234 Ill. Dec. 215



October 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Second District Appellate Court of Kane County. Nos. AC2-96-0956, AC2-96-0957, TR96MH285, TR96MH287. Honorable James C. Hallock, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a decision of the Second District Appellate Court of Kane County (Illinois), which reversed a trial court decision involuntarily committing appellee patient and authorizing the involuntary administration of medication. The lower court remanded the matter based on the public defender's waiver of the patient's right to be at the hearing. The lower court declared the statute under which she was committed unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the lower court was correct in reversing the trial court's judgments but that the lower court erred in pronouncing 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-806 (1996) unconstitutional. The trial court's judgments were infirm because the requirements of the Mental Health Code were not satisfied. The trial court allowed the proceeding to go forward without the patient, who was found subject to involuntary admission and psychotropic medication against her will. The public defender's appearance was problematic because the patient did not want him to represent her and claimed to be represented by someone else. The patient was presumed competent. When presented with information that the patient had secured alternative representation and rejected representation by the public defender, the trial court should not have ignored the matter. It should have delayed action on the commitment and medication issues pending a determination as to the status of her legal representation and her capacity to decide who should represent her. Because the sole witness to testify for the state had not examined the patient, 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-806(a) (1996) was not satisfied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court as far as it reversed the involuntary commitment but reversed the lower court's judgment as to the constitutionality of the statute under which the patient was involuntarily committed. The court reversed the trial court's judgments involuntarily committing the patient.
