People v. Espinoza


Docket No. 85050


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 252; 702 N.E.2d 1275; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1561; 234 Ill. Dec. 372



October 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing November 30, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. TR96CF1898. Honorable John L. Petersen, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) that dismissed for defendant the count for aggravated battery under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-4(b) (1994), and the counts for armed violence under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33A-2 (1994) based on the finding that the penalties imposed for those offenses violated the proportionate penalties clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970).


OVERVIEW: After defendant allegedly struck an individual with a bottle, he was charged with one count of attempted first degree murder, two counts of armed violence, one count of mob action, and one count of aggravated battery. The circuit court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the aggravated battery count and the armed violence counts because they were identical, yet had disproportional punishments. State contested and the court reversed the dismissal of those counts. The court remanded this case to resume proceedings against defendant on all counts. The court ruled that the proportionate penalties clause was violated when two offenses had identical elements, but were in different sentencing ranges. The court determined that that armed violence, predicated on the commission of aggravated battery (public way), was comprised of three primary statutory elements. In contrast, aggravated battery under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-4(b), was comprised of two such elements. Thus, the armed violence offenses charged in the second and third counts were not identical to the aggravated battery offense charged in the fifth count. Hence, the holding in the precedents did not require the dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court challenged by state, which dismissed the statutory aggravated battery count and the statutory armed violence counts brought against defendant. The circuit court incorrectly found that the potential penalties for those offenses did not violate the constitutional proportionate penalties clause. The court remanded the matter to proceed further.

Gem Elecs. of Monmouth, Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue


Docket No. 83203


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


183 Ill. 2d 470; 702 N.E.2d 529; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1567; 234 Ill. Dec. 189



October 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Fourth District Appellate Court of Sangamon County. Nos. AC4-96-0181, TR94MR0253.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant telecommunications repeater (repeater) sought review of a judgment of the Fourth District Appellate Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) which reversed a trial court decision setting aside appellee Department of Revenue's (Department) assessment of excise taxes against the repeater under the Telecommunications Excise Tax Act (Act), 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 630/1 et seq. (1992), and denied the repeater's claim for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The Department assessed excise taxes against the repeater on the ground that the repeater, by its function of amplifying and rebroadcasting existing FM signals, was taxable as a telecommunications receiver under § 3 of the Act, codified at 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 630/3 (1992). The trial court reversed the Department's assessment. The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment. On the repeater's appeal, the court held that: (1) under 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 630/3 (1992), the repeater received telecommunications, the repeater's customers purchased telecommunications from the repeater at retail, and the repeater was a retail seller; (2) the Act was not unconstitutionally vague because the repeater, by its hypothetical, did not carry its burden of clearly establishing the unconstitutionality of the Act; and (3) the repeater failed in its claim for attorney fees under § 55(c) of the Illinois Administrative Procedure Act, codified at 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 100/10-55(c), because the Department did not exceed its statutory authority in promulgating an administrative rule that included a repeater within the definition of retailer for purposes of the Telecommunications Excise Tax Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the Department.

People v. Shaw


Docket No. 80378


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


186 Ill. 2d 301; 713 N.E.2d 1161; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1562; 239 Ill. Dec. 311



October 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 1, 1999.
Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Shaw, 1999 Ill. LEXIS 687 (Ill., June 1, 1999)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Johnson, 315 Ill. App. 3d 1237, 777 N.E.2d 1093, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 4586, 268 Ill. Dec. 170 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion denied by People v. Shaw, 2016 IL App (3d) 140200-U, 2016 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 860 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Williams, 181 Ill. 2d 297, 692 N.E.2d 1109, 1998 Ill. LEXIS 5, 229 Ill. Dec. 898 (1998)



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed in part and vacated in part; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the Circuit Court (Illinois) judgment that convicted him pursuant to a theory of accountability of armed robbery under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-2(a) (1996), felony murder under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(3) (1996), first degree (knowing) murder under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1) (1996), and first degree (intentional) murder under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted pursuant to a theory of accountability of armed robbery under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-2(a) (1996), felony murder under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(3) (1996), first degree (knowing) murder under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1) (1996), and first degree (intentional) murder under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1) (1996). On appeal, the court reversed defendant's convictions for armed robbery and felony murder. The court found that accountability for felony murder existed only if defendant was deemed legally responsible for the felony that accompanied the murder. Because defendant was not accountable for the armed robbery, the court held that neither could he be held accountable for any murder occurring during the robbery. The court, therefore, reversed defendant's felony-murder and armed robbery convictions. Because the jury based its capital punishment sentence upon defendant's conviction for armed robbery, the court vacated defendant's death sentence. The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder because the evidence was clear that defendant aided in the death of the victim. The case was remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for armed robbery and felony murder because there was no evidence that he intended to aid the commission of a felony; and affirmed his convictions for first degree murder because the evidence showed that defendant knew that his associate intended to murder the victim. The court also vacated defendant's death sentence because it was erroneously based on his armed robbery conviction.

Russell v. Dep't of Natural Res.


Docket No. 84162


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


183 Ill. 2d 434; 701 N.E.2d 1056; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 932; 233 Ill. Dec. 782



October 1, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. TR96MR21. Honorable Robert J. Eggers, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of natural resources (department) and its director sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which declared § 3.36(a) of the Wildlife Code (Code), 520 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/3.36(a) (1994), to be unconstitutional because it was impermissibly vague and which reversed a department order, issued pursuant to § 3.36(a), which suspended appellee hunter's hunting privileges for three years.


OVERVIEW: The hunter pleaded guilty to four violations of the Code. The department filed an administrative complaint, pursuant to § 3.36(a), which provided that a license or permit issued under the Code could be revoked for up to five years if the person holding it were found guilty of any Code violation. The hunter requested an administrative hearing, claiming that § 3.36(a) was unconstitutional. The hearing officer rejected the hunter's claim and recommended that the hunter's hunting privileges be suspended for three years. The department adopted the hearing officer's report, and the hunter sought certiorari review in the circuit court. The circuit court judgment was reversed. The court held that § 3.36(a) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the hunter. The language of § 3.36(a) was sufficiently clear to provide a person of ordinary intelligence with fair notice that, if found guilty of a Code violation, the department could revoke and suspend that person's hunting privileges for up to five years. After applying the rational basis test in each instance, the court also rejected the hunter's claim that § 3.36(a) violated substantive due process and equal protection.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order declaring the statutory provision to be unconstitutionally vague was reversed. The court also reversed the circuit court's order directing the department to issue the hunter his permit or license.

People v. Burton


Docket No. 80726


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 1; 703 N.E.2d 49; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 934; 234 Ill. Dec. 437



October 1, 1998, Opinion Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree murder after a fitness hearing in which the parties stipulated to the testimony of two psychiatrists. The defendant waived a jury for sentencing and was sentenced by the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois to death. The defendant sought review of his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was hired by a couple's son to kill the couple. After the murder the defendant, the son and an accomplice confessed to the murders. People v. McLaurin


Docket No. 81487


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 58; 703 N.E.2d 11; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 920; 234 Ill. Dec. 399



September 24, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 26, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2929.
Rehearing denied by People v. Mc Laurin, 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1594 (Ill., Nov. 30, 1998)
Writ of certiorari denied McLaurin v. Illinois, 526 U.S. 1091, 119 S. Ct. 1506, 143 L. Ed. 2d 659, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2929 (1999)
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. McLaurin, 218 Ill. 2d 551, 850 N.E.2d 811, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 424, 303 Ill. Dec. 6 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. TR93CR5045. Honorable Paul J. Nealis, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions and sentences affirmed in part and vacated in part; death sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of first degree murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(1) (1989), felony murder under para. 9-1(a)(3), home invasion under para. 12-11(a)(2), aggravated arson under para. 20-1.1, residential burglary under para. 19-3(a), and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: The court vacated defendant's residential burglary and aggravated arson convictions because they were based on the same physical acts as his home invasion and intentional murder convictions. The court affirmed defendant's intentional murder, home invasion, and possession of a stolen motor vehicle convictions. The court held that defendant's convictions were supported by sufficient evidence because the accomplice witness' testimony was corroborated and other evidence linked defendant to the crime. It was not error for the trial court to refuse to compel the presence of defendant's witnesses because he did not make a plausible showing of how the testimony would have been material and favorable to his defense and it was not reasonably likely that it would have affected the outcome of the case. The court held that defendant's intelligent, voluntary, knowing waiver of his right to counsel was not error. The court affirmed defendant's death penalty because the aggravating factor in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(11) (1991) provided sufficient guidelines for the sentencer in determining death eligibility and the state only needed to prove one statutory aggravating factor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's intentional murder and home invasion convictions because the accomplice witness' testimony was corroborated, the trial court's refusal to compel the presence of immaterial defense witnesses was not error, and even capital defendants have the right to self-representation. The court reversed defendant's burglary and arson convictions because they were based on the same physical acts as other convictions.

 

46 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Lumpkin v. Cassidy


Docket No. 83289


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


184 Ill. 2d 117; 703 N.E.2d 1; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 930; 234 Ill. Dec. 389



September 24, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 30, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. TR94CH0229. Honorable Melvin E. Dunn, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted appellee lawn sprinkler installer's summary judgment motion and denied the State's summary judgment motion in the State's action, pursuant to the Illinois Plumbing License Law (Law), 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 320/0.01 et seq. (1996), to enjoin the installer from using laborers rather than licensed plumbers to install lawn sprinkler systems.


OVERVIEW: The installer used licensed plumbers to install backflow prevention devices (valves) but not to install pipes and sprinkler heads. The installer argued that because a properly installed valve effectively eliminated the risk that the potable water supply would be contaminated, requiring that licensed plumbers also be used to install the pipes and sprinkler heads did nothing to advance the purpose of the Law, violated the substantive due process guarantees of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, and contravened Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13's prohibition against special legislation. On appeal, the court noted that the presence of the valve did not render deficiencies in the piping system irrelevant from a public health standpoint; beyond avoiding contamination of potable water, requiring the use of licensed plumbers served the broader objective of protecting the public health, convenience, and welfare by affording greater protection to consumers; and the statute provided consumers with significantly greater recourse in the event of a problem. The licensure requirement was thus rationally related to a legitimate state goal, and that was all the constitutions required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court declaring the Illinois Plumbing License Law unconstitutional as applied to the installer and granting summary judgment in his favor. The court remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

47 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bowen


Docket No. 83687


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


183 Ill. 2d 103; 699 N.E.2d 577; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 919; 232 Ill. Dec. 800



August 6, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Adams County, the Hon. Mark A. Schuering, Judge, presiding. CASE NUMBERS: AC4-96-0275, TR95CF200.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant allegedly sexually assaulted a three-year-old girl. The girl's videotaped testimony was admitted as evidence pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-10(b)(1) (1994). After a bench trial, defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault and sentenced to nine years imprisonment. The Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) confirmed the conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the admission of the videotape was a violation of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-10 (1994) or of his rights under the confrontation clause, and that the state failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court affirmed. The mere omission from 5/115-10 of an express provision for videotaping did not reflect an intention to completely bar videotaped evidence. With regard to the impact on defendant's rights, there was little difference between introducing the statement on videotape or allowing it to be recounted in detail through the testimony of a third party. 5/115-10 made the introduction of the statements expressly contingent upon the child's production for direct and cross-examination at trial. In addition, the mandate that the child actually testify at trial, rather than merely being made available for testimony was of constitutional significance. Defendant had ample opportunity to explore any inconsistencies effectively on cross-examination. There was ample evidence demonstrating that the abuse occurred. Defendant failed to show that the evidence was so improbable or unsatisfactory that it warranted reversal of his conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault.

 

48 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wright


Docket No. 82866


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


183 Ill. 2d 16; 697 N.E.2d 693; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 909; 231 Ill. Dec. 908



June 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court. Kane County. CASE NUMBERS: TR96CF963. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Judith M. Brawka.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state made a direct appeal of an order from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which quashed a no-knock search warrant and suppressed the evidence seized during the execution of the warrant in a drug and firearm related criminal case.


OVERVIEW: Police officers had been given a no-knock search warrant for defendant and his home. The no-knock provision was granted based on information that easily accessible firearms were within the home. Defendant argued that 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/108-8(b)(1), which allowed for no-knock entries on that basis, was unconstitutional. The court agreed with defendant and held § 5/108-8(b)(1) unconstitutional. The mere presence of firearms to protect drugs did not create a valid exigent circumstance for the issuance of a no-knock warrant. Instead, police were required to show a reasonable belief that the weapons would be used against them if ordinary announcements were given. The court also rejected the state's argument that the fruits of the search should not be suppressed because the police acted in good faith reliance of the validity of the search warrant. Although a federal "good faith" exception to the U.S. Const. amend. IV exclusionary rule existed, that exception did not extend to the exclusionary rule found at Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 (1970).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling that the exigent circumstance portion of the statute was unconstitutional. The court also affirmed the ruling that the unannounced entry by police was unreasonable under constitutional standards. Finally, the court affirmed the order quashing the search warrant and suppressing the evidence seized.

Zimmerman for Zimmerman v. Skokie


Docket No. 82893


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


183 Ill. 2d 30; 697 N.E.2d 699; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 910; 231 Ill. Dec. 914



June 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court. Cook County. CASE NUMBERS: AC1-94-2448, TR91L4831. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Warren D. Wolfson.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed in part; circuit court judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury verdict in favor of defendants village and police officers in this action for injuries sustained by plaintiff arrestee, the appellate court (Illinois) affirmed an order of the trial court granting the arrestee's motion for a new trial. The appellate court also held that the operation of the special duty doctrine to negate legislatively provided immunities was not unconstitutional. The village and police officers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee suffered permanent brain damage following a suicide attempt while he was held in jail. His parents had told the police that their son was claustrophobic and could not tolerate confinement. This action was brought on his behalf by his court appointed guardian. The trial court dismissed the negligence count of the complaint, and the remaining claims proceeded to trial; the jury found in favor of the village and the officers. The trial court then granted the arrestee's motion for a new trial. The appellate court affirmed this grant and rejected the officers' argument that the special duty doctrine violated the Illinois Constitution of 1970 when it was applied to override the immunities afforded by the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/1-101 et seq. (Act). The court held that such doctrine violated the provisions on sovereign immunity, Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 4, and the separation of powers, art. II, § 1. This was because the special duty doctrine was a judicially created exception to the public duty doctrine and could not contravene the immunities provided to governmental entities under the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the arrestee that the operation of the special duty doctrine was not unconstitutional.

People v. Sanders


Docket No. 82917


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


182 Ill. 2d 524; 696 N.E.2d 1144; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 911; 231 Ill. Dec. 573



June 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court. Lake County. CASE NUMBERS: TR96CV1099.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was charged with violating 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 125/2(c) (1996) of the Illinois Hunter Interference Prohibition Act. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) dismissed the charge against the defendant, finding that the statutory section was impermissibly vague and overbroad in violation of the United States Constitution. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was charged with interfering with the lawful taking of a wild animal in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 125/2(c) (1996) after he disturbed another individual by yelling at her and taking her photograph as she attempted to shoot a deer. The defendant argued that the statutory section was overbroad in violation of the First Amendment and unconstitutionally vague in violation of the Due Process Clause. The state argued that the statute was neither overbroad nor vague. On appeal, the court found that in evaluating the statute, proper interpretation had to be given to the term "dissuade." The court held that subjecting the defendant to criminal liability for expression that was intended to dissuade the lawful taking of a wild animal, while failing to threaten punishment for expressions intended to encourage or persuade, constituted an illegal legislative censure of opinion that was not content-neutral. The court held that the prohibitions of the section did not serve a compelling state interest and that the unconstitutional section was severable from the remaining potions of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the circuit court, which dismissed the case against the defendant, after finding that the statutory provision from the Illinois Hunter Interference Prohibition Act was a content-based regulation not justified by a compelling state interest.

People v. Johnson


Docket No. 79923


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


182 Ill. 2d 96; 695 N.E.2d 435; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 364; 230 Ill. Dec. 945



April 16, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied June 1, 1997.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him in part of two counts of murder and sentenced him to death under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(3) due to a prior conviction for murder. Part of defendant's argument was that the trial court should not have under § 9-1(b)(3) used a murder that was committed after the instant murder and that his confession should have been suppressed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant while being interrogated for one murder confessed to another for which he was also charged. Upon his conviction for the instant murder, the trial court, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(3), imposed the death sentence due to his prior conviction for the other murder. On appeal defendant argued that the trial court should not have used under § 9-(b)(3) a murder on which he had been previously convicted but which in fact he committed after the offense for which he was being sentenced. The court rejected that argument, holding that the statute referred to prior convictions, not prior crimes, and the fact that murder convictions may occur out of sequence did not make the statute unconstitutionally arbitrary, violate due process or apply the statute ex post facto. Neither did the police violate Ill. Const. 1970, art. I, § 2, § 3, or § 10 because defendant was not denied access to his attorney during interrogation in which the court found he knowledgeably waived his rights prior to his confessions. The court dismissed all of defendant's arguments as to the death penalty statute's unconstitutionality with little discussion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of two counts of murder and sentenced him to death. The court held that it was correct to use a prior murder conviction as a basis for the death sentence even though the other offense occurred after the murder for which he was being sentenced. The court also rejected the claim that the confessions were obtained in violation of the Illinois Constitution.

People v. Jackson


Docket No. 79243


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


182 Ill. 2d 30; 695 N.E.2d 391; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 361; 230 Ill. Dec. 901

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant's murder conviction and death sentence were remanded to the lower court. On remand to the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), the jury found the defendant eligible for the death penalty and that sentence was imposed. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. On remand for resentencing, the trial court again imposed the death penalty and the defendant appealed. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the defendant's rights were not violated by the trial court's voir dire of the prospective jurors. The court resolved many evidentiary issued against the defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and set a date for the imposition of the death sentence against the defendant.

Woods v. Cole


Docket No. 82895


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


181 Ill. 2d 512; 693 N.E.2d 333; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 355; 230 Ill. Dec. 204



March 19, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court. Morgan County. Case Numbers: AC4-96-0345, TR93L27. Trial Judge: Hon. Tim P. Olson.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate brought a wrongful death action against defendant tortfeasor. The tortfeasor asserted that if he were found liable for the decedent's death, he would have the right under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1117 to have his liability apportioned relative to the liability of other tortfeasors involved in the death. On interlocutory appeal, the appellate court concluded that § 2-1117 was inapplicable, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The estate alleged that the decedent was killed after the tortfeasor had negligently entrusted a firearm to another and had acted in concert with others in pointing and discharging the firearm at the decedent. The sole issue on appeal was whether § 2-1117 was applicable in negligence actions where several tortfeasors acted "in concert" to cause a single, indivisible harm. The court held that the section was not applicable under such circumstances. The court held that § 2-1117 required, as a threshold matter, that the liability of the tortfeasors be capable of being legally apportioned. If the liability could not be legally apportioned, then § 2-1117 would not come into play. The court noted that it was legally impossible to apportion liability among tortfeasors who acted in concert, and, therefore, § 2-1117 could not apply to cases where the tortfeasors acted in concert to cause the injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court.

Dowd & Dowd, Ltd. v. Gleason, 284 Ill. App. 3d 915, 672 N.E.2d 854, 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 798, 220 Ill. Dec. 37 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1996)

The judgment appealed from denied defendants' requests for sanctions and summary judgment in an action plaintiff law firm brought that sought to impose a constructive trust on the income of a firm started by defendants, who were plaintiff's ex-employees.

Conspiracy count simply represented an alternative theory of liability.

Graham v. Illinois State Toll Highway Auth.


Docket Nos. 83491, 83492, 83662 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


182 Ill. 2d 287; 695 N.E.2d 360; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 360; 230 Ill. Dec. 870



March 19, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied June 1, 1997.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiff class of persons that used the toll highway system, defendant state officials appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ruled that the provisions of the Toll Highway Act, 605 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/24 and 10/25 authorizing spending without an annual appropriation violated the Illinois Constitution of 1970 and enjoined them from paying any expense other than debt service.


OVERVIEW: The class of users of the toll highway system filed an action for injunctive and declaratory relief, alleging that, in violation of Ill. Const. of 1970, art. VII, § 2, the governor had not budgeted, and the General Assembly had not appropriated for, any expenditures of funds defendant Illinois State Toll Highway Authority by the Authority for the fiscal year. The circuit court found the Toll Highway Act violated the 1970 Constitution and ordered injunction on spending. On direct appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the method of spending set forth in the Toll Highway Act did not violate the 1970 Constitution. The court relied on its prior decisions which upheld various aspects of the predecessor statute to the Toll Highway Act against challenges based upon provisions of the 1870 Constitution. The predecessor statute's spending provision was identical in pertinent part to that contained 605 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/24 and 10/25. The drafting history of Ill. Const. of 1970, art. VIII, § 2(b), clearly indicated that § 2(b) was not intended to alter the prior holding of the court upholding the constitutionality of the Toll Highway Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court holding the Toll Highway Act unconstitutional and preliminarily enjoining any disbursements was reversed on the grounds that the Illinois Constitution of 1970 did not prohibit the legislature from authorizing the method of spending contained in the Toll Highway Act.

 

58 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Devine v. Murphy


Docket No. 82965


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


181 Ill. 2d 522; 693 N.E.2d 349; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 359; 230 Ill. Dec. 220



March 19, 1998, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ granted in part and denied in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of Illinois reviewed petitioner attorney's petition for a writ of mandamus in which the attorney requested the court to order respondent judges to vacate their orders holding 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/23-15 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The principal modification of prior law made by the revision of § 23-15 was the abolition of the judicially created doctrine known as constructive fraud. Under the new § 23-15, the property tax assessment adopted by the appeal boards was presumed to be correct and legal. However, this presumption could be rebutted by clear and convincing evidence. The trial court, under the new § 23-15, was to hear the objection to the property tax assessments de novo and determine whether the assessment was incorrect or illegal. The court found that the power of the legislature to broaden the right of judicial review of property tax assessments beyond fraud or constructive fraud was clearly warranted by the language of article VI, section 9, of the Illinois Constitution. Because considerable deference was still given to the decisions made by the board of review or appeals, and the only powers granted to the courts under § 23-15 was the power to consider a matter which fell within the reviewing province of the courts, no separation of powers violation was found and the statute was deemed constitutional.


OUTCOME: After finding § 23-15 constitutional, the court granted that portion of the petition for writ of mandamus which requested an order to the judges to vacate their orders holding § 23-15 unconstitutional.

 

59 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Watts


No. 81548


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


181 Ill. 2d 133; 692 N.E.2d 315; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 350; 229 Ill. Dec. 542



February 20, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Lake County. Case Numbers: AC2-95-0762, TR94CF1754. Trial Judge: Hon. John R. Goshgarian.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee was convicted of home repair fraud under the Home Repair Fraud Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 515/3(a)(1) (1994), and acquitted of other charges in the Lake County Court (Illinois). The appellate court reversed the conviction and the state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court determined that the intent presumption of the Home Repair Fraud Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 515/3(a)(1) (1994), was mandatory. It told the fact finder that it had to assume the existence of intent if the state proved the existence of the factors listed in the statute, unless the presumption was rebutted. The appellate court concluded that once the presumption of intent was triggered, the burden of persuasion shifted to appellee to disprove the element of intent. The appellate court determined that the state was collaterally estopped from retrying appellee for home repair fraud because, in a retrial, the trial court would have had to decide whether appellee intended to perform the home repairs without the aid of the statutory presumption. The court held that the presumption portion of the Home Repair Fraud Act was unconstitutional. Because the court invalidated the presumption, a court in a retrial under the Act would be left to determine the issue of appellee's intent precisely as it was decided under the theft count at the original trial. Because that issue has been decided once, it could not be relitigated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court which reversed appellee's conviction for home repair fraud under the Home Repair Fraud Act.

County Collector v. Anvan Midwest (In re County Collector)


Docket No. 84160


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


181 Ill. 2d 237; 692 N.E.2d 264; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 341; 229 Ill. Dec. 491



February 20, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DuPage County. Case Numbers: TR93TX1-040, TR93TX10040. Trial Judge: Hon. John W. Darrah.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers filed objections to an application of appellee tax collector for judgment for delinquent 1992 real estate taxes. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) denied the objectors' motion for partial summary judgment and overruled objections to a bond levy. The taxpayers appealed and the intermediate court transferred the appeal to the court pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 365.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 245/1-7(b) (1992) violated the contract clause under U.S. Const., art. I, § 10, and Ill. Const. art. I, § 16 by impairing a park district's ability to refund preexisting debt instruments. On appeal the court held that: (1) the fundamental principle of statutory construction was to look to the words of a statute, (2) 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 245/1-5 (1992) of the Property Tax Extension Limitation Act (act), 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 245/1-1 et seq. (1992), provided that taxes included in an aggregate extension were subject to a property tax extension limitation unless approved by referendum or otherwise excluded, (3) exclusion 3 under 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 245/1-5 (1992) excluded extensions to pay interest or principal on bonds issued to refund or continue to refund those bonds issued before the effective date of this act, (4) because a park district's extensions used to pay preexisting obligations were excluded from the aggregate extension, the extensions were not subject to the act's cap, (5) the trial court had not erred when it granted a rehearing on a legal issue, (6) interested parties were properly permitted to intervene.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that denied the taxpayers' motion for partial summary judgment and overruled objections to a tax district's bond levy because tax extensions used to "refund" bonds issued before the effective date of a tax cap referendum statute were not subject to a statutory cap.

 

61 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


R.W. Dunteman Co. v. C/G Enters.


Docket Nos. 81853, 82184 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


181 Ill. 2d 153; 692 N.E.2d 306; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 346; 229 Ill. Dec. 533



February 20, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cook County. Case Numbers: TR96CH6152. Trial Judge: Hon. Albert Green.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that held the Mechanics Lien Act § 1.1, 770 Ill. Comp. Stat. 60/1.1 (1992), to be unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff entered into a written contract with the city to perform certain roadwork. Plaintiff then entered a subcontract agreement with defendants to perform certain services. During the course of construction, the city became dissatisfied with defendants' performance and directed plaintiff to remove them from the project. Defendants then filed a mechanics lien against the monies due plaintiff from the city. The city advised plaintiff that funds would not be released because of the lien claims. Thereafter, plaintiff filed a complaint for declaratory judgment, requesting a determination that the lien claims were void and unenforceable. The trial court found the Mechanics Lien Act § 1.1, 770 Ill. Comp. Stat. 60/1.1 (1992), to be unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court held that § 1.1 was not unconstitutionally vague. Therefore, the court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court. The court found that the language of the statute was unambiguous. The court further found that it was evident from the language of the statute that the legislature intended to prohibit provisions waiving the right to a mechanic's lien because such provisions were against public policy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a decision of the trial court holding that the Mechanics Lien Act was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the statute was unambiguous and clearly provided that the legislature intended to prohibit provisions waiving the right to a mechanic's lien because such provisions were against public policy. The court therefore remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

62 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Cincinnati Ins. Co. v. Chapman


Docket Nos. 83223, 83241, 83312, 83404 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


181 Ill. 2d 65; 691 N.E.2d 374; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 10; 229 Ill. Dec. 264



February 3, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] No. 83404-Judgment affirmed. Nos. 83223 & 83241-Motions granted. No. 83312-Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff movants sought supervisory orders from the court directed against defendant judges and court clerks to declare the Judicial Redistricting Act of 1997 (Act) unconstitutional. Defendants claimed that all sections of the Act were constitutional except those which related to Cook County, and that the constitutional portions of the Act were severable from the unconstitutional portions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff movants sought a supervisory order from the court to declare that the Judicial Redistricting Act of 1997 (Act) was unconstitutional. The court declared the statute unconstitutional and void. The court affirmed a trial court's finding that the provisions of the Act which impacted Cook County were invalid. The court held that the provisions of the Act that redistricted judicial districts two through five were unconstitutional in that they improperly split several judicial circuits amongst multiple judicial districts in violation of Ill. Const. 1970, art. VI. The court found that both the legislative history and the debates supported plaintiffs' assertion that the presumption of severability created by the insertion of a severability clause in the Act was rebutted. The court found that the overwhelming intent of the legislature was to reconfigure the entire state judiciary in order to rectify certain perceived constitutional irregularities and as such, all of the Act's provisions were "inextricably bound."


OUTCOME: The court held that the Judicial Redistricting Act of 1997 was unconstitutional and that its constitutional provisions were not severable from the unconstitutional provisions. The court held that the Judicial Redistricting Act of 1997 was void in its entirety. The court granted the supervisory orders requested that reflected the determination of unconstitutionality and denied the remainder of the relief sought.

People v. Cortes


No. 80149


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


181 Ill. 2d 249; 692 N.E.2d 1129; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1; 229 Ill. Dec. 918



January 23, 1998, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Convictions affirmed in part and vacated in part; death sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of four counts of first degree murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 9-1, and two counts of armed robbery in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 18-2, and imposed a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant told his friends that he was going to rob the two victims. Defendant later told his friends that he had shot the victims and that he possessed cash, gold jewelry, a compact disc player, and CD cassettes that had been taken from them. Both victims were found dead with gunshot wounds to their heads. Property had been taken from their apartments. Defendant was convicted of four counts of murder. The trial court sentenced defendant to death. Defendant claimed on appeal that he was denied effective assistance of counsel by his attorney's failure to demand a fitness hearing based upon his ingestion of psychotropic drugs, that the state improperly introduced evidence of prior crimes, and that the death sentence was improper. The court rejected defendant's claims but found that defendant could not be found guilty of four counts of murder when only two murders had occurred. The court found that defendant was fit for trial based upon evidence presented at a post-conviction fitness hearing, that defendant interjected his ability to understand English, and that the state properly introduced evidence from previous convictions during which defendant was able to communicate in English.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's two convictions for intentional murder. The court vacated defendant's convictions for two felony murders because they were based upon the same conduct that supported the intentional murder convictions. The court affirmed defendant's death sentence.

 

64 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Department of Children & Family Servs. v. People (In re A.A.)


Docket Nos. 81711, 81800 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


181 Ill. 2d 32; 690 N.E.2d 980; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 3; 228 Ill. Dec. 905



January 23, 1998, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Children and Family Services sought review of the judgment of the trial court, which declared the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2-10 and 2-27 unconstitutional under the Equal Protection Clauses of the Illinois and United States Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: An order was entered finding a delinquent minor to be neglected, and he was made a ward of the lower court. Appellant Department of Children and Family Services was appointed guardian and received custody. Appellant sought reconsideration of the custody order, arguing that because the minor was over the age of 13 and had previously been adjudicated delinquent, he was statutorily ineligible for placement in the custody of appellant under the Juvenile Court Act of 1987 (Act), 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2-10 and 2-27. Appellee state responded that the Act violated the Equal Protection Clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The trial court agreed and concluded that there was no rational basis for preventing the class of minors 13 years of age or older adjudicated delinquent from receiving custodial care by appellant. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the Act did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because the legislature could rationally distinguish between teenaged minors whose need for shelter was directly related to their delinquency and those whose delinquency was independent from the basis for finding abuse, neglect, or dependency.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order of the trial court, holding that the Juvenile Court Act of 1987 did not violate the Equal Protection Clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The court held that the legislature could rationally conclude that other available placement options, not under the authority of appellant Department of Children and Family Services, were sufficient to provide for the needs of the ineligible minors.

People v. Branning (in Re Branning)


Docket No. 82662


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


1998 Ill. LEXIS 6



January 23, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by In re Branning, 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1929 (Ill., Mar. 30, 1998)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Branning (In re Branning), 285 Ill. App. 3d 405, 674 N.E.2d 463, 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 948, 220 Ill. Dec. 920 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 1996)



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Illinois sought review of the appellate court's decision to grant appellee disabled person's motion to dismiss the trial court's authorizing electroconvulsive therapy without appellant's consent under 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-110 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was under guardianship because of mental illness. The guardian consented to treat appellant with electroconvulsive therapy and filed a petition seeking approval of her consent under 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-110 (1994). Appellant challenged the trial court's approval of the electroconvulsive therapy, and the appellate court found the statute unconstitutional. The court affirmed the appellate court's decision. The case was moot, but the court decided because issues arising under the statute were capable of repetition, yet evaded review. Appellant had standing because she was in immediate danger of sustaining a direct injury as a result of enforcement of the statute. The court held that the statute was unconstitutional because it lacked necessary basic protections. The court held that the statute did not provide for a standard of proof, provide for a determination regarding a patient's capacity to make a rational decision regarding treatment, list specific conditions that might require treatment, provide for a determination that the benefits of treatment outweighed potential harm, weigh less restrictive alternatives, or provide a time limit for the termination of treatment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision denying the guardian's petition to admit electroconvulsive therapy to appellant without consent because the statute was facially unconstitutional. The statute did not provide for a standard of proof, provide for a capacity determination, list conditions that might require treatment, provide for a determination that benefits outweighed potential harm, or discuss less restrictive treatments.

People v. Williams


Docket No. 80377


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


181 Ill. 2d 297; 692 N.E.2d 1109; 1998 Ill. LEXIS 5; 229 Ill. Dec. 898



January 23, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 30, 1998.
Modified by, Rehearing denied by, 03/30/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Williams v. Illinois, 525 U.S. 882, 142 L. Ed. 2d 157, 119 S. Ct. 192, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 5785 (1998)
Related proceeding at People v. Shaw, 186 Ill. 2d 301, 713 N.E.2d 1161, 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1562, 239 Ill. Dec. 311 (1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Williams, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 369 (Ill., Mar. 18, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which sentenced him to death following his conviction for first degree murder in the shooting death of a police officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder in the shooting death of a police officer. The jury sentenced defendant to death and found no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude imposition of that sentence. On direct appeal, the court affirmed and found, from the totality of the circumstances, that defendant's statements to a paramedic regarding the shooting were voluntary. 67 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Best v. Taylor Mach. Works


Docket Nos. 81890, 81891, 81892, 81893 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


179 Ill. 2d 367; 689 N.E.2d 1057; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 478; 228 Ill. Dec. 636; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,123



December 18, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Madison County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. David R. Herndon. Case Numbers: TR96L167, TR96L182.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a railroad, an engineer, and manufacturers, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court, Madison County (Illinois), which declared unconstitutional the Civil Justice Reform Amendments of 1995 (Act). The Act made changes in tort recovery, liability, and procedure. Plaintiff injured workers had sought a declaration of the Act's unconstitutionality in their respective suits.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that the following provisions of the Act violated the Illinois Constitution: (1) the limitation on compensatory damages for noneconomic injury, (2) § 3.5(a) of the Joint Tortfeasor Contribution Act (740 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 100/3.5(a) (1996)), (3) the abolition of joint and several liability, and (4) discovery statutes which mandated unlimited disclosure of a plaintiff's medical records. Because these unconstitutional provisions could not be severed from the remainder of the Act, the Act as a whole was rendered invalid. The injured workers' complaint challenging the constitutionality of the Act portended the ripening seeds of litigation because they alleged a sufficient and direct interest in the application of the challenged provisions of the Act to their lawsuits. The court applied the rational basis test. The Act was based upon anecdotal evidence of dubious verity and interfered with the injured workers' constitutional rights in its differing treatment of injured plaintiffs as to its recovery cap and its limitations on joint contribution. The Act also interfered with privacy rights in its mandatory disclosure of all medical information and records.


OUTCOME: The court vacated that portion of the circuit court's holding that reached the substantive merits of the products liability issues and the jury instructions, but otherwise affirmed the judgment of the circuit court in its entirety.

 

68 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Fletcher v. Williams


Docket Nos. 81599, 81600, 81601 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


179 Ill. 2d 225; 688 N.E.2d 635; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 465; 227 Ill. Dec. 942



November 20, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2390.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court, Lee County. CASE NUMBERS: TR96MR32, TR96MR26, TR96MR25. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Tomas M. Magdich.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Illinois Prison Review Board members (board) appealed a declaration from the Circuit Court of Lee County (Illinois) that held 730 ILCS 5/3-3-5(f) (1996) of the Unified Code of Corrections, unconstitutional as an ex post facto law. The circuit court enjoined the board from scheduling plaintiff inmates' subsequent parole hearings less frequently than once per year.


OVERVIEW: The board after it denied the inmates parole rescheduled their next parole hearing three years later pursuant to 730 ILCS 5/3-3-5(f) (1996) of the Unified Code of Corrections. The court reversed the judgment below after interpreting Ill. Const. art. I, § 16 (1970), Illinois' ex post facto prohibition, based upon the United State Supreme Court's interpretation of the ex post facto prohibition contained in U.S. Const. art. I, § 9. The court held that the Supreme Court's change of its ex post facto analysis reversed that part of the court's decision in Tiller v. Klincar, 138 Ill. 2d 1, 149 Ill. Dec. 206, 561 N.E.2d 576 (1990), that applied the Miller-Weaver-Lindsey test of ex post facto lawmaking. Consequently, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat 5/3-3-5(f) was not ex post facto because it did not increase the inmates' punishment, it affected the inmates only after the first parole hearing and the board concluded that the inmates could not have reasonably expected to have been paroled until the scheduled rehearing, and because the board could tailor the frequency to new facts raised by the inmates.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that held an amended statute that permitted the board to schedule the inmates' subsequent parole hearings at less than once per year was an ex post facto law. The court held that the amended statute did not increase the inmates' punishment, and so was not unconstitutional.

Richardson v. Rock Island County Officers Electoral Bd.


Docket No. 82136


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


179 Ill. 2d 252; 688 N.E.2d 633; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 470; 227 Ill. Dec. 940



November 20, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court, Rock Island County. CASE NUMBERS: AC3-96-0902, TR96MR195. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Martin E. Conway, Jr.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee voter filed a petition to add a referendum to an election ballot. Appellant individuals objected to the petition and appellant county electoral board (board) denied the petition due to an insufficient number of signatures on appellee's petition. Appellee sought review and the Circuit Court, Rock Island County (Illinois) set aside the board's decision. Appellants sought review and the appellate court transferred the case to the court.


OVERVIEW: The petition sought to place a referendum on the ballot to dissolve a township. The circuit court held that the provision of the township code that prescribed the procedure for determining the validity of a petition to initiate a referendum was unconstitutionally vague and uncertain because a petitioner could not ascertain the number of signatures required prior to filing since the minimum number of signatures was determined on the date the petition was filed, and thus created a moving target. The court dismissed the appeal as moot because by the time they heard the case the election had passed and the referendum had not been on the ballot due to a stay issued by the appellate court. There was no need for an authoritative determination for future guidance and the issue was not likely to recur because by the time the case reached the court, the Illinois General Assembly had amended the provision of the township code that was held invalid by the circuit court. The amendment removed the ostensibly unconstitutional language while the case was pending and the amendment foreclosed the possibility that the issue would recur in a future case.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal as moot.

Kunkel v. Walton


Docket No. 81176


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


179 Ill. 2d 519; 689 N.E.2d 1047; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 468; 228 Ill. Dec. 626



November 20, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court, Macon County. CASE NUMBERS: TR95L288. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Scott B. Diamond.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant physicians appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Macon County (Illinois), which entered an order holding that 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1003(a) (1994) was unconstitutional. The physicians had served plaintiffs, a patient and her husband, with a request for consents to authorize the release of medical information pursuant to § 2-1003(a), in the action of the patient and her husband seeking recovery for medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: A patient and her husband filed a medical malpractice action against physicians. The physicians served the patient and her husband with a request for consents authorizing the release of medical information pursuant to § 2-1003(a). The patient and her husband sought a protective order, challenging the constitutionality of § 2-1003(a). The trial court entered an order declaring § 2-1003(a) unconstitutional. The physicians appealed that determination. The court held that § 2-1003(a) placed no limitation whatsoever on the scope of medical information that was subject to disclosure, as the procedure for consenting to disclosure of medical information went well beyond the legitimate objectives of discovery as reflected in the court's rules. Thus, § 2-1003(a) represented an impermissible encroachment upon the judicial branch's authority. The trial court also correctly held that § 2-1103(a) violated the right to privacy set forth in the state constitution, as the statute required a blanket consent to disclosure of all medical information without regard to the issues being litigated. The scope of the required disclosure was unreasonable and unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court holding that the statute requiring consent forms from injured parties authorizing the release of medical information was unconstitutional.

Marsh v. Ill. Racing Bd.


Docket No. 80913


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


179 Ill. 2d 488; 689 N.E.2d 1113; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 469; 228 Ill. Dec. 692



November 20, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court, First District, Cook County. CASE NUMBERS: AC1-96-0523, TR96CH729. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Lester D. Foreman.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff horse racer challenged an order of the Appellate Court, First District, Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant racing board's emergency motion on interlocutory appeal to stay the circuit court's order. The circuit court had entered an order that stayed the racing board's decision pending judicial review of the racing board's decision to revoke the horse racer's license and make him ineligible for future licensure.


OVERVIEW: The horse racer argued that the circuit court's stay order was not appealable under Sup. Ct. R. 307(a)(1). 166 Ill. 2d R. 307(a)(1). The court found that the circuit court's stay order entered pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-111(a)(1) (1994) was interlocutory in nature and could not be deemed a final order for purposes of appeal. However, the court found that the injunctive nature of the order was entitled to appellate review under Sup. Ct. R. 307(a)(1) to ensure that the circuit court granted the relief in accordance with the statutory criteria. Accordingly, the court found that the appellate court had jurisdiction over the appeal of the circuit court's entry of the stay order. The court found that the appellate court did not decide the issue of the circuit court's stay on the merits but granted the racing board the stay and remanded the matter. The court noted that the order resembled either an order issued pursuant to some supervisory power, which the appellate court lacked, or a summary order, which was improper. The court remanded to the appellate court for a determination of the merits of the racing board's appeal.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's order and remanded the cause to the appellate court for further proceedings not inconsistent with its opinion.

Stern v. Norwest Mortg.


Docket Nos. 82412, 82512 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


179 Ill. 2d 160; 688 N.E.2d 99; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 455; 227 Ill. Dec. 762



October 23, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 1, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court, First District of Cook County. Case Numbers: AC1-95-1627, TR93CH05220. Hon. Albert Green, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagors and defendant mortgagee both appealed from a judgment entered by the Appellate Court, First District of Cook County (Illinois), which found in favor of the mortgagors on their claim under the Mortgage Escrow Account Act (Escrow Act), 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. 910/1 et seq. (1992), and against them on their claim under the Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act (Fraud Act), 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 505/2 (1992).


OVERVIEW: The mortgagors obtained a loan from the mortgagee. Under the Escrow Act, the mortgagors had the option of pledging an interest-bearing deposit in lieu of the mortgagee's establishment of an escrow account in order to cover the payment of anticipated taxes. When the mortgagors chose the deposit option, the mortgagee charged an escrow waiver fee. The mortgagors filed suit and alleged that the mortgagee was barred from charging such a fee, and that the mortgagee misrepresented the provisions of the Escrow Act in violation of the Fraud Act. The court held that § 6 of the Escrow Act, specifically 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. 910/6, prohibited the mortgagee from charging the escrow waiver fee. The court further held that prohibiting such a fee was not federally preempted by the Depository Institutions Deregulation and Monetary Control Act of 1980, 12 U.S.C.S. § 1735f-7a. Furthermore, the Escrow Act was not unconstitutionally vague or a violation of the separation of powers doctrine. However, the court also found that the mortgagors failed to state a cause of action under the Fraud Act because there was no evidence that the charging of the fee was an attempt to deceive or defraud the mortgagors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower appellate court, which found in favor of the mortgagors on their Escrow Act claim but dismissed the mortgagors' Fraud Act claim for failure to state a cause of action.

Milwaukee Safeguard Ins. Co. v. Selcke


Docket No. 82047


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


179 Ill. 2d 94; 688 N.E.2d 68; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 462; 227 Ill. Dec. 731



October 23, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Case Numbers: TR93CH9266, TR93CH9268, TR93L50663, TR93L50665, TR93L50674, TR93L50699, TR93L50972, TR93L50974, TR93L50976, TR93L50988, TR93L51000, TR93L51038, TR93L51040, TR93L51042, TR93L51066, TR93L51373, TR93L51377, TR94L50629, TR93CH9267, TR93CH9269, TR93L50664, TR93L50668, TR93L50698, TR93L50971, TR93L50973, TR93L50975, TR93L50977, TR93L50999, TR93L51001, TR93L51039, TR93L51041, TR93L51057, TR93L51371, TR93L51374, TR94L50419, TR94L50915. Hon. Randye A. Kogan, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, insurance director and state treasurer, challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted partial summary judgment for plaintiff foreign insurance companies in their facial constitutional challenge to 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/409 (1992) and their demand for a refund.


OVERVIEW: The insurance director and the state treasurer contended that the trial court erred in declaring 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/409 (1992) unconstitutional and that there were genuine issues of material fact precluding summary judgment. The court held that to survive scrutiny under the uniformity clause of Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970), a nonproperty tax classification had to be based on a real and substantial difference between the people taxed and those not taxed and had to bear some reasonable relationship to the object of the legislation or to public policy. The court held that imposing the 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/409 (1992) privilege tax on all foreign insurance companies did not bear a reasonable relationship to the object of the legislation or to public policy. Imposing the privilege tax on foreign companies solely because they were not incorporated in Illinois was an impermissible use of the Illinois legislature's taxing power. Accordingly, the court held that 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/409 (1992) violated Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970). Also, the court held that there were no genuine factual disputes precluding summary judgment in this case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of partial summary judgment for the foreign insurance companies and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

City of Chicago v. Morales


No. 80479, 80485, 80668 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


177 Ill. 2d 440; 687 N.E.2d 53; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 451; 227 Ill. Dec. 130



October 17, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Granted April 20, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2516.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with violating the City of Chicago's Gang Congregation Ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 8-4-015. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss the city's actions against them, finding the ordinance unconstitutionally vague. An Illinois appellate court affirmed, holding the ordinance unconstitutional. The city sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, suspected gang members, were charged with violating the gang loitering ordinance after they refused to comply with police orders to disperse. The charges were dismissed on constitutional grounds. The court affirmed the determination that the ordinance was impermissibly vague and violated defendants' substantive due process rights. The court held that the freedom to engage in harmless activities was an aspect of the personal liberties protected by the due process clause, U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV, and included the general right to travel, the right to freedom of movement, and the general right to associate with others. The court held that where an underlying statute was impermissibly vague, as the gang loitering ordinance was, defendants could not be convicted based upon failure to obey the order of a police officer pursuant to that ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of charges, holding that the gang loitering ordinance was an arbitrary restriction on personal liberty and violated substantive due process.

People v. Love


Docket No. 82104


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


177 Ill. 2d 550; 687 N.E.2d 32; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 454; 227 Ill. Dec. 109



October 17, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. John F. Michela, CASE NUMBERS: AC3-95-0937, TR94CF712.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, the appellate court (Illinois) determined that the trial court's order directing that defendant's bond money be used to pay for the cost of his public defender was improperly entered, and remanded for a hearing. The state sought leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with several crimes, and a relative posted bond securing his release. After conviction, the trial judge summarily ordered that the public defender be paid from the bond. The appellate court reversed the order. On appeal by the state, in affirming the decision reversing the order for payment, the court held that constitutional principles required that reimbursement be ordered only when certain conditions were satisfied. The trial court's failure to adhere to the procedural safeguards mandated by 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/113-3.1 (1994) required vacatur of the reimbursement order, despite defendant's failure to object. At a hearing on the issue, special consideration had to be given to third parties who posted bond on the defendant's behalf.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court vacating the order directing that defendant's bond money, which had been posted by a third party, be paid to the public defender and remanding for a hearing concerning defendant's ability to pay.

East St. Louis Fed'n.of Teachers, Local 1220 v. East St. Louis Sch. Dist. No. 189 Fin. Oversight Panel


Docket No. 81077


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


178 Ill. 2d 399; 687 N.E.2d 1050; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 450; 227 Ill. Dec. 568



October 17, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. Hon. Robert L. Craig, Trial Judge. Case Number TR95CH0193.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State of Illinois and the Illinois State Board of Education, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which held that an emergency financial assistance statute was unconstitutional and that actions taken to remove plaintiffs, the superintendent of a school district and school board members, were void.


OVERVIEW: The superintendent of a school district and the school board filed an action against the state and the state board of education, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief. Specifically, they sought to enjoin the removal of the members of the school board from office, and they sought a declaratory judgment that an emergency financial assistance statute was unconstitutional. The lower court held that the statute was unconstitutional and that actions taken to remove the members of the school board were void. On appeal, the court found that the statute was valid on its face. The court further found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. Its terms were capable of sufficiently precise interpretation by a person of ordinary intelligence. However, the court found that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to the school board members for failure to provide the members with procedural due process before their removal from office.


OUTCOME: The order finding the emergency financial assistance statute unconstitutional was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

77 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Bruso by Bruso v. Alexian Bros. Hosp.


Docket Nos. 81369, 81451, 81474 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


178 Ill. 2d 445; 687 N.E.2d 1014; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 441; 227 Ill. Dec. 532



October 2, 1997, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, hospital and physicians, sought review of a judgment of an Illinois appellate court, which reversed an order of the trial court and found that the medical malpractice lawsuit of plaintiff minor, who was mentally incompetent, was not barred by the statute of limitations, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-212 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff minor sued defendants, hospital and physicians, for injuries he allegedly suffered at the time of his birth. Plaintiff, who was mentally incompetent as a result of his injuries, filed suit 16 years after his birth. The trial court dismissed plaintiff's action, finding that it was barred by the eight-year statute of limitations for medical malpractice suits filed by minors, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-212 (1994). The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court and held that plaintiff's action was not barred by the statute of limitations. The court held that where a plaintiff in a medical malpractice action was a minor and was also under another legal disability such as mental incompetency, the plaintiff's action was subject to the tolling provision of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-212(c) (1994) and not the eight-year repose period of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-212(b) (1994). The court also held that defendants did not have standing to pursue an equal protection challenge to the statute because they were not members of the class against whom the statute allegedly discriminated, mentally competent minors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment. The statute of limitations did not bar plaintiff minor's action against defendants, hospital and physicians, because plaintiff was mentally incompetent. The court held that where plaintiff was a minor and under another legal disability, namely mental incompetency, plaintiff's action was subject to a tolling provision for those under legal disabilities and not the eight-year repose period for actions by minors.

People v. Woolley


Docket No. 79483


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


178 Ill. 2d 175; 687 N.E.2d 979; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 433; 227 Ill. Dec. 497



September 25, 1997, Opinion Filed

Rehearing denied by People v. Woolley, 1997 Ill. LEXIS 877 (Ill., Dec. 1, 1997)
Writ of certiorari denied Woolley v. Illinois, 524 U.S. 955, 118 S. Ct. 2375, 141 L. Ed. 2d 742, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 4336 (1998)
Subsequent appeal at People v. Woolley, 205 Ill. 2d 296, 793 N.E.2d 519, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 282, 275 Ill. Dec. 748 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Woolley v. Gaetz, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 77158 (C.D. Ill., July 30, 2010)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in an Illinois circuit court of murder, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1), (a)(2), (a)(3), armed robbery, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-2(a), robbery, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-1(a), and unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-1.1. Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The defendant appealed his convictions for murder, armed robbery, robbery, and unlawful possession of a weapon on several grounds including the ground that the circuit court erred in denying his motion to suppress his confession because the police violated his right to counsel during custodial interrogation. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for murder, armed robbery and unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, reversed the defendant's conviction and sentence for robbery, and vacated the death sentence and remanded the case to the circuit court for a new capital sentencing hearing.

Murneigh v. Gainer


Docket Nos. 81195, 82042 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


177 Ill. 2d 287; 685 N.E.2d 1357; 1997 Ill. LEXIS 430; 226 Ill. Dec. 614



September 18, 1997, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former prisoner brought an action against defendants, state police director, former corrections director, and warden, challenging the constitutionality of 730 Ill. Comp Stat. § 5-4-3(i) (1994) and the two implementing regulations. The circuit court granted summary judgment for plaintiff, enjoined defendants from seeking a blood sample from him, and expunged a previously taken sample. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff refused to voluntarily give defendants a blood sample. Defendants sought to punish him by contempt of court under § 5-4-3(i). Defendants argued that res judicata barred the challenge to § 5-4-3(i) and that § 5-4-3(i) and the two implementing regulations increased the judiciary's contempt power, by facilitating the courts' exercise of such power. The court held that the circuit court's order invalidating § 5-4-3(i) and the regulations as violating the separation of powers doctrine was correct and that the provisions were severable from the remaining portions of the legislation. The provisions compelled the judiciary to enter orders that were administrative in nature and then to punish violations of such orders with contempt of court in violation of the separation of powers doctrine of Ill. Const. of 1970, art. II, § 1. The court rejected defendants' res judicata argument because in a prior appeal the court expressly declined to resolve whether § 5-4-3(i) was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment that granted summary judgment to plaintiff which enjoined defendants from seeking a blood sample and expunged a previously taken sample.
