OUTCOME: The court vacated one of defendant's convictions for home invasion but affirmed his remaining convictions and his death sentence.

 

130 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Miller


Docket No. 78983


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


171 Ill. 2d 330; 664 N.E.2d 1021; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 41; 216 Ill. Dec. 93



March 28, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County, the Hon. Alford R. Penniman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Boone County (Illinois), which dismissed an information charging defendant with concealing a fugitive in violation of § 31-5 of the Criminal Code of 1961, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/31-5, on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional under the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: The fugitive defendant concealed was a class A misdemeanant. The misdemeanant was subject to a penalty of less than one year's confinement and a fine not to exceed $ 1,000. By contrast, defendant's concealment offense could be punished by a penalty of up to one to three years' confinement and a fine not to exceed $ 10,000. In reversing the judgment that dismissed the information, the court held that this scheme of punishment did not offend the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The court held that the legislature could reasonably have concluded that concealing a fugitive was a more serious offense, in some circumstances, than the offense the fugitive committed. The court also held that the legislature could reasonably have concluded that concealment of a misdemeanant, a felony, was a more serious offense that aiding a misdemeanant's escape, which was a misdemeanor. The court also held that the offense applied to concealment of a misdemeanant, as it was addressed at concealing an "offender," which encompassed those who broke any penal law, misdemeanor or felony.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which dismissed the information that charged defendant with concealment.

 

131 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Jacobson v. Department of Pub. Aid


Docket No. 78880


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


171 Ill. 2d 314; 664 N.E.2d 1024; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 42; 216 Ill. Dec. 96



March 28, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, the Hon. Alford R. Penniman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Public Aid (Department) determined that appellee parents were liable for the support of their 19-year-old daughter pursuant to the Illinois Public Aid Code, specifically 305 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/10--2 (1992). The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) affirmed a circuit court decision setting aside the decision based on constitutional considerations. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The question presented to the court was whether § 5/10-2 violated equal protection as guaranteed by Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970) and the Fourteenth Amendment because there was no rational basis for its imposition of financial responsibility on parents of 18- to 20-year-old children where the children resided in the parents' home while exempting from liability parents whose children resided elsewhere. The court held that the statute did violate the equal protection clauses because there was no rational basis for the distinction found in 305 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/10-2. It reasoned that because the idea of public aid was to redistribute resources from those who have the ability to contribute to those who are in need, the residence of a child was immaterial. The dispositive factor was the parents' financial condition. The ability to pay for a child's support was not necessarily gauged by whether or not the parent agreed to allow an 18- through 20-year-old child to reside with him. Furthermore, § 5/10-2 did not serve to strengthen family unity and was directly at odds with the stated purpose of the Code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the statute violated equal protection but modified the judgment by striking only the unconstitutional portions of the section, leaving constitutional subparts in place.

Jarabe v. Industrial Comm'n (American Airlines)


Docket No. 79666


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


172 Ill. 2d 345; 666 N.E.2d 1; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 43; 216 Ill. Dec. 833



March 28, 1996, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Circuit court judgment reversed; Commission decision confirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee parents challenged an arbitrator's award of benefits for their daughter's death, which was affirmed by appellant Industrial Commission (Commission) under § 7(i) of the Worker's Compensation Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 305/7(i). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) declared the statute unconstitutional and the Commission appealed.


OVERVIEW: An employee was killed during the course of her employment, and her dependant parents were the beneficiaries of her worker's compensation death benefits. The arbitrator applied § 7(i), which reduced the weekly death benefit amount by 50 percent because the beneficiaries were non-resident aliens living in the Philippines. The Commission affirmed the award. The parents filed suit and the circuit court reversed, holding that § 7(i) was unconstitutional. During the pendency of the matter the mother died and her estate became a party. The Commission appealed, and the court reversed the judgment of the circuit court. It held that the Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses applied to citizens and resident aliens; non-resident aliens did not have standing to raise constitutional claims. It rejected the claim that the parents were standing in the shoes of their deceased daughter and could assert her rights. It held that beneficiaries under the Worker's Compensation Act (Act) had no rights derivative of the deceased employee, and that the personal cause of action of the beneficiary or dependant under the Act arose on the death of the employee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court judgment and confirmed the decision of the Commission in the award of reduced death benefits to the non-resident alien parents of a deceased employee.

Allegro Servs. v. Metropolitan Pier & Exposition Auth.

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


172 Ill. 2d 243; 665 N.E.2d 1246; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 44; 216 Ill. Dec. 689



March 28, 1996, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff transportation businesses appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment on the pleadings or summary judgment in defendant authority's favor on each of the counts in plaintiffs' class action complaint.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff transportation businesses included several suburban and out-of-state businesses that provided bus, van, or limousine transportation from the airports, but which did not service destinations within the city. Plaintiffs brought a class action against defendant authority challenging the constitutionality of the airport departure tax imposed by defendant under the Commerce Clause and the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution and the Uniformity Clause of the Illinois Constitution. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of defendant on all counts. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the tax did not violate the Equal Protection Clause or the Uniformity Clause because defendant submitted a legally sufficient justification for imposing the airport departure tax on the bus and van operators in the plaintiff classes. The court held that plaintiffs failed to meet their burden of introducing evidence to show that the asserted justifications for taxing members of plaintiff classes were factually erroneous. The court held, as to all plaintiffs' arguments, that the tax comported with the requirements of the interstate Commerce Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which dismissed all counts in plaintiffs' class action complaint.

People v. Brown


Docket No. 74532


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


172 Ill. 2d 1; 665 N.E.2d 1290; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 37; 216 Ill. Dec. 733



March 28, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 3, 1996.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him on three counts of first degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of and sentenced to death for the murders of a woman and her two young children. Defendant appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and the sentence. First, assuming that trial counsel was deficient at the suppression hearing, at the guilt phase, and at sentencing, the court did not believe that defendant was prejudiced as a consequence of the alleged deficiencies, or that the deficiencies would have affected the outcome of the trial. With respect to the sentence, the court found any errors harmless, and that the death penalty statute, 38 Ill. Rev. Stat. 9/1 (1989), did not unconstitutionally impose on defendant a burden of establishing that a noncapital sentence should have been imposed.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant for three counts of first degree murder and imposing the death sentence was affirmed.

Tully v. Edgar


Docket No. 80076


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


171 Ill. 2d 297; 664 N.E.2d 43; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 26; 215 Ill. Dec. 646



March 21, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered judgment in favor of plaintiff complainant in his declaratory judgment action, thereby finding Ill. Public Act 89--5 unconstitional.


OVERVIEW: The Act changed the process of selecting trustees to the board of the state university from an elective process to an appointive process. The Act provided that the terms of the elected trustees who were in office on the effective date of the Act were to terminate on a certain date. Complainant initiated a declaratory judgment action against the governor, contending that the Act was unconstitutional because it violated the right to vote found in Ill. Const. art. III. The trial court found that the Act was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found that the provision of the Act terminating the elective trustees' terms prior to expiration was unconstitutional. The court reasoned that the Act essentially nullified votes cast in a valid election by removing trustees from office midterm. The state was unable to identify any compelling state interest that justified the midterm removal of trustees and replacing them with appointed trustees. The court found that the remaining portions of the Act were constitutional and severable from the removal portions of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that found the portion of the Act regarding removal of elected trustees was unconstitutional. The court reversed the decision that found the remaining portions of the Act unconstitutional.

People v. Simpson


Docket No. 76889


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


172 Ill. 2d 117; 665 N.E.2d 1228; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 28; 216 Ill. Dec. 671



March 21, 1996, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), which convicted him of first degree murder and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially represented by the public defender. Despite being informed by the trial judge that his counsel had not had time to prepare, defendant persisted in his demands for immediate trial. The trial court granted defendant's request to proceed pro se. On appeal, defendant alleged, inter alia, that his waiver of his Sixth Amendment right to counsel was not knowingly and intelligently made. The court noted that the record indicated that defendant was literate, responsive, and understanding. It was clear that he was familiar with the provisions of the speedy-trial statute. It was reasonable to conclude that defendant knew that the case against him could be dismissed if not brought to trial within the statutory period. Therefore, defendant was motivated to forego continuances to avoid extending the period within which the State was obliged to bring him to trial under the speedy-trial statute. The trial court was not required to readmonish defendant of his right to counsel prior to the sentencing hearing. Although defendant may have committed a tactical error during the trial, this did not demonstrate his lack of ability to waive counsel.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court was affirmed.

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS

March 21, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court of appeal from an order of the Illinois Human Rights Commission.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a married couple, sought review of a decision by the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) that affirmed a judgment finding that respondent employer's no-spouse policies in the workplace did not violate the Illinois Human Rights Act, 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-101 et seq. (1992).


OVERVIEW: After a couple in the same department of the employer's workplace announced their intent to marry each other, they were informed that an unwritten policy prohibited married couples from working on the same shift, in the same area. The couple contended that the no-spouse policy in the workplace was discriminatory under the Illinois Human Rights Act (Act), 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-101 et seq. (1992). The court held that (1) the statutory definition of marital status discrimination did not encompass policies based on the identity of the married couple; (2) had the legislature intended to include an individual's relationship to another within the protected classes of the Act, it would have done so in specific and certain terms; and (3) an administration's interpretation of an unambiguous statute was not entitled to deference.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 2151 et seq. (1989).


OVERVIEW: In the department's action to collect taxes against the drug dealer under the Cannabis and Controlled Substances Tax Act (Act), the trial court declared that the statute was invalid and could not be applied where the party from whom the tax was sought had already been convicted and sentenced on criminal charges involving the same contraband. People v. DiLorenzo


Docket No. 78372


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


169 Ill. 2d 318; 662 N.E.2d 412; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 21; 214 Ill. Dec. 846



February 15, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. Joe Vespa, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for aggravated criminal sexual abuse. He challenged the affirmation of his conviction by the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), claiming that the indictment under which he was charged was unconstitutionally defective.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by indictment with criminal sexual assault, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and aggravated criminal sexual abuse, under Ill. Rev. The appellate court determined that an indictment was sufficient, because it apprised defendant of the precise offense charged with enough specificity to prepare his defense and to allow pleading a resulting conviction as a bar to future prosecution arising out of the same conduct, and held that the indictment against defendant in the case at bar was not constitutionally deficient.

People v. Whitehead


Docket Nos. 71791, 77379 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


169 Ill. 2d 355; 662 N.E.2d 1304; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 24; 215 Ill. Dec. 164



February 15, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 1, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Grundy County, the Hon. Louis J. Perona, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Grundy County (Illinois) which denied his petitions filed under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-1 et seq. (1981), seeking relief from his conviction and death sentence for murder and aggravated kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death for the aggravated kidnapping and murder of a five-year-old girl. The trial court denied defendant's petitions for relief filed under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court did not err by dismissing defendant's claim of trial counsel's ineffectiveness. Counsel was not ineffective for withdrawing defendant's insanity defense, for failing to introduce evidence that the husband of the woman with whom defendant was having a baby had a motive to frame defendant, or for failing to introduce more mitigating evidence at sentencing. Given the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt, including his eight confessions and lack of remorse at the sentencing hearing, it was not reasonable that the result would have been different. Defendant's right to an impartial jury under U.S. Const. amend. VIII was not violated by the facts that the juror's names and addresses were published in the local newspaper or by the jurors' observation of the victim's mother's outburst against defendant. Defendant's due process rights were not violated by a juror's use of a line scale to weigh the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel or his rights to an impartial jury or due process.

People v. Oaks


Docket No. 75541


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


169 Ill. 2d 409; 662 N.E.2d 1328; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 25; 215 Ill. Dec. 188



February 15, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 1, 1996.
Rehearing denied by, 04/01/1996
Writ of certiorari denied Oaks v. Illinois, 519 U.S. 873, 117 S. Ct. 191, 136 L. Ed. 2d 129, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 5553 (1996)
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Oaks, 221 Ill. 2d 662, 857 N.E.2d 680, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1378, 306 Ill. Dec. 281 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Oaks v. Williams, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 104284 (C.D. Ill., Aug. 10, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Henry County, the Hon. Jeffrey W. O'Connor, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Henry County (Illinois) that convicted him of two counts of first degree murder and one count of aggravated battery of a child for the death of his girlfriend's three year old son and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree murder and one count of aggravated battery of a child for the death of his girlfriend's three-year-old son. The trial court found defendant eligible for the death penalty because the victim was under 12 years of age and the death resulted from exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. 1991, ch. 38, par. 9-1(b)(7). On appeal the defendant raised a number of arguments. The court found that (1) each of the counts in the indictment set forth the statutory elements for that offense, (2) the indictment was no duplicitous, (3) the defendant's statements were noncustodial and voluntarily made, (4) evidence of prior injuries was admissible to show the presence of intent or knowledge and the absence of accident, (5) the evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction of murder, (6) there was no error in the instructions, (7) the jury needed the expert testimony to determine if the injuries were intentional or accidental, (8) the murder was exceptionally brutal and heinous, and (9) there could only be one conviction for murder.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for knowingly killing the three-year-old child was affirmed, and the felony murder conviction was vacated. The clerk of the court was directed to enter an order setting the date on which the death sentence was to be carried out.

 

142 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Henderson


Docket No. 75948


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


171 Ill. 2d 124; 662 N.E.2d 1287; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 14; 215 Ill. Dec. 147



January 25, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 1, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas E. Deyer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who had been sentenced to death, appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that dismissed, without an evidentiary hearing, his petition for relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1989, ch. 38, par. 122--1 et seq. Alternatively, he sought remand for a new trial, or remand for a new sentencing hearing, or remand for an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death for participating in the victim's gang rape and then transporting her in the trunk of his car to a place where he stabbed her 40 times and then ran over her body. The court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court's "rehabilitative potential" standard, which the trial court used when it determined defendant's sentence, was vague and arbitrary and violated his rights under U.S. Const. amends. VIII and XIV. The court ruled that the standard itself was acceptable and that the trial court took many other factors into consideration as well when it imposed the death sentence. The court ruled that defendant did not demonstrate that he received ineffective assistance of counsel because many of the instances the defendant argued should have been raised by counsel in mitigation appeared actually to be aggravating factors, or at least to have strong aggravating components. The court ruled that it was not error to reject defendant's contention that his confession had been physically coerced. The court ruled that the trial court's refusal to hold a post conviction evidentiary hearing or allow submission of additional expert testimony was not error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed defendant's post-conviction claims. The court set May 22, 1996, as the date for defendant's execution.

People v. Hooper


Docket No. 76068


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


172 Ill. 2d 64; 665 N.E.2d 1190; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 15; 216 Ill. Dec. 633



January 25, 1996, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of armed robbery under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18--2 (1979), aggravated kidnapping under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10--2(a)(3), and murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--1(a)(1), and sentenced him to death for the murder convictions, after a second sentencing hearing, and denied his motion for a new sentencing hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18--2 (1979), aggravated kidnapping under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10--2(a)(3), and murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--1(a)(1). On review, the court vacated the death sentence imposed for the murder convictions, and after second sentencing hearing in the circuit court, the defendant was again sentenced to death. His motion for a new sentencing hearing was denied, and he appealed the sentence. The court affirmed the sentence of death, holding that the evidence and the state's comments regarding all five of the murders committed by defendant did not prejudice defendant in either the eligibility or aggravation and mitigations phases, because it was incumbent upon the state to demonstrate the intent or knowledge necessary pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9--1(b)(3), and because the jury was able to consider any reliable evidence relevant to aggravation or mitigation. In addition, the court held that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to have precluded the imposition of a sentence of death, and therefore, would not disturb the circuit court's order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order, which sentenced defendant to death for his convictions for murder, holding that defendant was not prejudiced in the eligibility phase or the aggravation and mitigation phase by the state's evidence and comments regarding both the murders for which defendant was being sentenced, and those committed in Arizona.

People v. Munson


Docket No. 76197


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


171 Ill. 2d 158; 662 N.E.2d 1265; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 16; 215 Ill. Dec. 125



January 25, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 1, 1996.
Rehearing denied by, 04/01/1996
Writ of certiorari denied Munson v. Illinois, 519 U.S. 880, 136 L. Ed. 2d 141, 117 S. Ct. 205, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 5649 (1996)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Munson, 206 Ill. 2d 65, 206 Ill. 2d 104, 794 N.E.2d 155, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 334, 276 Ill. Dec. 260 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Munson v. McAdory, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 6405 (N.D. Ill., Apr. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Shelvin Singer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted the defendant of first-degree murder, aggravated kidnapping, armed robbery, and arson of property, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a), 10-2(a)(5), 18-2(a), 20-1(a) (1991). The trial court sentenced the defendant to death for the murder conviction and to concurrent prison terms for the other convictions. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant and a friend got into the victim's car and forced him to drive to a remote area. They robbed the victim and shot him, then set fire to the car. The victim's body was discovered by off-duty paramedics. On appeal, the court held that (1) the trial court did not err in finding that the state's explanations for two of its peremptory challenges were race-neutral and that the defendant had failed to prove pretext, (2) the defendant failed to establish an ineffective assistance of counsel claim because he did not demonstrate prejudice, (3) the trial court properly considered statutory and nonstatutory aggravating factors, along with the deterrent effect of punishment, in imposing the death penalty, (4) there was no plain error in the state's closing argument, (5) the trial court did not err in failing to appoint new counsel to represent the defendant on his post-trial pro se ineffective assistance of counsel motion because the defendant provided no factual or legal basis for the claim, and (6) Illinois's death penalty statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 (1991), was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's convictions and sentences.

People v. Moore


Docket No. 75813


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


171 Ill. 2d 74; 662 N.E.2d 1215; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 10; 215 Ill. Dec. 75



January 18, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 1, 1996.
Rehearing denied by, 04/01/1996
Writ of certiorari denied Moore v. Illinois, 519 U.S. 875, 117 S. Ct. 195, 136 L. Ed. 2d 132, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 5577 (1996)
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Moore, 189 Ill. 2d 521, 727 N.E.2d 348, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 315, 245 Ill. Dec. 95 (2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Moore, 2012 IL App (3d) 100696-U, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1119 (2012)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Moore v. Hardy, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28046 (N.D. Ill., Feb. 25, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Grundy County, the Hon. Robert H. Adcock, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Grundy County (Illinois) that convicted him of seven counts of first degree murder, and one count each of home invasion, residential burglary, aggravated criminal sexual assault, robbery, and arson and sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, home invasion, residential burglary, aggravated criminal sexual assault, robbery, and arson and was sentenced to death. The court affirmed his conviction and sentence. There was sufficient evidence to convict him of murder beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant waived his claim to challenge the admissibility of DNA evidence and any error that the trial court made in denying defendant's request for a hearing was harmless due to the overwhelming evidence of his guilt. Defendant was not denied a fair trial and due process by prosecutorial comments concerning forensic evidence, the presumption of innocence, and his failure to testify. Defendant was also not denied effective assistance of counsel because there was no evidence that counsel's alleged failures prejudiced him. Further, defendant was not denied a fair capital sentencing hearing because the trial court denied his request to argue jury nullification, permitted the introduction of hearsay evidence, and did not check allegedly inflammatory comments by the state in closing arguments. Finally, the court refused to reconsider the constitutionality of Illinois' death penalty statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder, home invasion, residential burglary, aggravated criminal sexual assault, robbery, and arson and his death sentence. The evidence was more than sufficient to convict him, and defendant's allegations of error either did not constitute error or did not constitute plain error. Finally, the court refused to reconsider the constitutionality of the death penalty statute.

People v. Brown


Docket No. 75556


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


169 Ill. 2d 132; 661 N.E.2d 287; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 11; 214 Ill. Dec. 433



January 18, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Cause remanded by People v. Brown, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 945 (Ill., Oct. 18, 2002)
Appeal after remand at People v. Brown, 204 Ill. 2d 422, 792 N.E.2d 788, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1416 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl E. Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Conviction affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him and sentencing him to death for murder. The trial judge found defendant eligible for the death penalty, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(b)(3), (b)(11) (1994), and further found that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude the imposition of a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was one of two men who allegedly shot the victim. The court affirmed the conviction, but reversed and vacated the death sentence. The court found, inter alia, that (1) defendant's inculpatory statements to police regarding the shooting were voluntary, and thus properly admitted, because under the totality of the circumstances defendant's will was not overborne at the time of the confession and evidence existed to show that his right to counsel was not invoked; (2) the evidence was sufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant caused the victim's death because his act did not need to be the sole or immediate cause of death, but rather it was sufficient that the act contributed to cause the death; (3) defendant's waiver of a jury for sentencing was invalid because, not only did the trial judge neglect to admonish defendant as to his right to a jury, he also misstated the law and affirmatively misled defendant into tendering the waiver prior to the conviction; and (4) defendant's death penalty eligibility was sufficiently proven where one separate, valid factor remained to support the eligibility after one of the aggravating factors was invalidated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, vacated the death sentence, and remanded the cause to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing.

 

147 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rodriguez


Docket No. 78135


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


169 Ill. 2d 183; 661 N.E.2d 305; 1996 Ill. LEXIS 1; 214 Ill. Dec. 451



January 18, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Loretta Hall Morgan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both the state and defendant appealed from a judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which upheld defendant's aggravated criminal sexual assault and intimidation convictions. The appellate court vacated the home invasion conviction on the basis that the home invasion and the aggravated criminal sexual assault were based on the same act.


OVERVIEW: Based on the common act of threatening the victim with a gun, the appellate court held that the two offenses were so interrelated that it was required to vacate the home invasion conviction. On appeal, the court reversed the vacation of the home rule conviction but affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated criminal sexual assault and intimidation. The court held that the aggravated criminal sexual assault offense and the home invasion offense were based on separate acts. Defendant's unlawful entry into the victim's bedroom was an overt or outward manifestation that supported a different offense, the home invasion. Also, the home invasion was not a lesser-included offense of the aggravated criminal sexual assault. The indictment referred to different conduct for each offense. In the aggravated criminal sexual assault counts, the state alleged that defendant committed an act of sexual penetration and displayed or threatened the victim with a gun. However, in the home invasion count, the state alleged that defendant unlawfully entered the victim's dwelling and threatened her with the imminent use of force while armed with a gun.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's vacation of the home invasion conviction. The court affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated criminal sexual assault and intimidation.

People v. Bounds


Docket No. 75687


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


171 Ill. 2d 1; 662 N.E.2d 1168; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 219; 215 Ill. Dec. 28



December 21, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 1, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas A. Hett, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Direct review was granted of defendant's judgment and sentence rendered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Defendant was found guilty by a jury of murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and aggravated kidnapping. The same jury found the defendant eligible for the death penalty and further determined that there were no mitigating circumstances sufficient to preclude imposition of that sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and aggravated kidnapping and the jury found defendant eligible for the death penalty. Defendant challenged his conviction on numerous grounds including validity of his confession, alleged errors in jury selection, alleged evidentiary errors, comments of the prosecutor, and the propriety of the death penalty. The court affirmed the judgment and imposition of the death penalty. The court held that there was no reason to disturb the trial court's ruling that defendant's signed confession was admissible. The court held that there was nothing in the jury selection process to find that the chosen jurors were prevented from the performance of their duties. The court found that there was evidence independent of defendant's confession to support the offenses of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping. The court held that the prosecutor's comments in the sentence phase were not inappropriate. The court upheld the constitutionality of the Illinois death penalty, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(e) (1989).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that found defendant guilty of murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and aggravated kidnapping. The court affirmed the trial court's finding that defendant was eligible for the death penalty and set a date for the sentence to be carried out.

Calloway v. Kinkelaar


Docket No. 77391


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


168 Ill. 2d 312; 659 N.E.2d 1322; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 223; 213 Ill. Dec. 675



December 21, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Effingham County, the Hon. Harold H. Pennock III, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff abused spouse filed an action against defendants, sheriff and county, for alleged willful and wanton or negligent failure to comply with the Illinois Domestic Violence Act of 1986 (Act), 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 60/101 et seq. (1992). The Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois) reversed the dismissal of the complaint as to the two counts alleging wanton and willful behavior. The sheriff and county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The abused spouse secured an order of protection against her husband under the Act, which prohibited tharassment of the abused spouse, entering her place of employment, or telephoning her at work. The sheriff personally served the order of protection on the husband. One morning, thereafter, the husband began calling the abused wife at work, threatening to kill himself in front of the abused wife and their child if she did not pick the child up from his house personally. The abused wife called the sheriff who drove by the house but did not stop or investigate further. Ultimately, the husband came to the abused wife's workplace, kidnapped her at gunpoint, and shot himself. The abused wife filed an action against the sheriff and the county for their failure to comply with the Act by failing to arrest the husband upon her first report of his unlawful acts or transporting her to a safe place. The court found that the Act created a right of action for the wanton and willful disregard of police duties under the Act, but that no cause of action for police negligence could lie under the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's reinstatement of those counts of the complaint sounding in willful and wanton misconduct. The court also affirmed the dismissal of the two counts of the complaint sounding negligence.

People v. Foster


Docket No. 75716


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


168 Ill. 2d 465; 660 N.E.2d 951; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 215; 214 Ill. Dec. 244



November 30, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing January 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. Barry E. Puklin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought relief pursuant the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-1 et seq., after his conviction for first degree murder was affirmed and his petition for writ of certiorari was denied. The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) dismissed defendant's post-conviction petition without an evidentiary hearing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in dismissing his post-conviction petition because his trial counsel (1) failed to present evidence to show that his confessions were not voluntary; (2) failed to present an intoxication defense and should have called lay and expert witnesses to testify about his state of mind; (3) and was ineffective for failing to subject the state's case to meaningful testing with regard to his commission of aggravated criminal sexual assault. The state argued that several of defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of trial counsel had been waived for failure to raise them on direct appeal. The court held that defendant's contentions were without merit. The court found that (1) defendant failed to show a likelihood that the trial judge would have suppressed his confessions if trial counsel had introduced additional evidence; (2) that there was no reasonable probability that testimony that defendant's drinking altered the functionality of his brain would have resulted in the granting of his motion to suppress; and (3) that it was unlikely that the additional evidence offered by defendant would have changed defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which dismissed defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

People v. Orange


Docket No. 75786


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


168 Ill. 2d 138; 659 N.E.2d 935; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 210; 213 Ill. Dec. 589



November 22, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Orange, 195 Ill. 2d 437, 749 N.E.2d 932, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 476, 255 Ill. Dec. 450 (2001)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Orange v. Burge, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 75103 (N.D. Ill., Sept. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas P. Durkin, Judge, presiding.
Orange v. Illinois, 488 U.S. 900, 109 S. Ct. 247, 102 L. Ed. 2d 235, 1988 U.S. LEXIS 4436, 57 U.S.L.W. 3260 (1988)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder, concealment of a homicidal death, and aggravated arson. When his murder and concealment convictions and death sentence were affirmed and after his petition for a writ of certiorari was denied, defendant filed a post-conviction petition for reversal of his conviction and a new trial. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the petition. Defendant appealed pursuant to 134 Ill. 2d R. 651(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a post-conviction petition under Ill. Rev. Stat. 1989, ch. 38, para. 122-1 et seq., after he was sentenced to death for murder and concealment of a homicidal death. The petition was dismissed. Defendant appealed under 134 Ill. 2d R. 651(a) and asserted that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel at trial in violation of his U.S. Const. amends. VI, XIV rights, denied the effective assistance of counsel at sentencing because defense counsel failed to investigate or present any mitigating evidence, and his jury waiver at sentencing was uninformed. The court held that defendant was not denied the right to effective counsel at trial because the evidence showed that the scope of defense counsel's investigation of a claim of police brutality as a basis for a motion to suppress defendant's confession was reasonable and that defense counsel presented an active defense, an evidentiary hearing was necessary on the allegation that defense counsel failed to adequately investigate mitigating evidence, and the evidence showed that defendant discussed the jury waiver with defense counsel, understood it, and voluntarily executed it.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence of death was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The case was remanded for an evidentiary hearing on the parts of the post-conviction petition that alleged a denial of the effective assistance of counsel due to trial counsel's failure to investigate and present mitigation evidence at the capital sentencing hearing.

People v. Simms


Docket No. 76430


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


168 Ill. 2d 176; 659 N.E.2d 922; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 209; 213 Ill. Dec. 576



November 22, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of DuPage County, the Hon. Ronald Mehling, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of DuPage County (Illinois) of numerous crimes including murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a) (1985), aggravated criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14(a) (1985), criminal sexual assault, and armed robbery, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18-2 (1985) and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed his convictions. The death sentence was stayed pending review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised numerous issues on appeal including a juror was improperly excused for cause, evidence of his past crimes violated his sixth amendment right to counsel, gang evidence was admitted in violation of his right to confrontation and freedom of association, and the prosecutor made improper statements during closing argument. On appeal, the court held (1) the juror was properly excused because he indicated that he could not be impartial regarding the death penalty, (2) the defendant waived his claim that his sixth amendment right to counsel was violated because his counsel made only a general objection to the evidence resulting in waiver of the claim, (3) evidence of defendant's gang association was properly admitted because it was relevant as evidence of defendant's character, (4) the prosecutor's statements in closing did not go beyond the bounds of proper argument because they were attempts to rebut the defendant' mitigation evidence, the remarks were isolated instances, and the judge instructed the jury that closing arguments were not evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and the death sentence.

People v. Coleman


Docket No. 75902


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


168 Ill. 2d 509; 660 N.E.2d 919; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 204; 214 Ill. Dec. 212



November 2, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Henry C. Tonigan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which denied him relief under the Post Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-1 et seq. (1991), from his conviction for aggravated kidnapping and murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised numerous claims alleging the ineffective assistance of counsel and errors by the trial court. The court held that (1) the trial court had not erred in its determination that defendant was competent to waive counsel because the trial court had found the testimony of a forensic psychiatrist lacked credibility and considered defendant's conduct during trial and lay opinions of other mental health professionals, (2) defense counsel was not ineffective in failing to assert a defense to the imposition of the death penalty based on Eighth Amendment proportionality principles because the omissions did not result in prejudice to defendant and based on the overwhelming evidence, there was no reasonable probability that the jury would have concluded differently if such question had been submitted, and (3) defense counsel was not ineffective for failure to conduct an investigation into defendant's personal background and mental or emotional condition for the purpose of mitigating evidence during the penalty proceedings because in light of the aggravating circumstances surrounding the crime, such evidence would not have been sufficient to change the jury's sentencing decision.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was affirmed. The clerk of the court was directed to enter an order setting the date for defendant's execution.

People v. Keene


Docket No. 76329


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


169 Ill. 2d 1; 660 N.E.2d 901; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 203; 214 Ill. Dec. 194



November 2, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 29, 1996.
Rehearing denied by, 01/29/1996
Writ of certiorari denied Keene v. Illinois, 519 U.S. 828, 117 S. Ct. 92, 136 L. Ed. 2d 47, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 4901 (1996)
Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Remanded by, in part People v. Keene, 399 Ill. App. 3d 1234, 990 N.E.2d 936, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 2436, 371 Ill. Dec. 748 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County, the Hon. Lawrence A. Smith, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Stephenson County (Illinois) convicted defendant of armed robbery and murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant directly appealed the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several challenges to his convictions and sentence. The court held: 1) that the refusal to pay for a pathologist to counter evidence that a left-handed person had slit the victim's throat did not violate due process and equal protection guarantees because that issue was not crucial to the defense; 2) that defendant was not entitled to dismiss a juror for cause as predetermined to vote for death when the juror indicated that he would not vote for death if he believed that the penalty was inappropriate; 3) that defendant's exclusion from the courtroom during a witness's voir dire did not violate his right to confront witnesses and his right to due process because it did not interfere with the opportunity for cross-examination at trial; 4) that the state did not impermissibly remark on defendant's failure to testify by stating that certain evidence was uncontradicted because the remarks referred to the "what," not the "who," of the evidence; and 5) defendant could not argue that his counsel was ineffective by failing to present a witness's statement when he failed to show that the statement would have been admissible at trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for armed robbery and murder was affirmed.

People v. Arna


Docket No. 77551


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


168 Ill. 2d 107; 658 N.E.2d 445; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 199; 212 Ill. Dec. 963



October 26, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. William Hibbler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed his convictions for attempted first degree murder and ordered the trial court on remand to impose consecutive, rather than concurrent, sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted murder for shooting his former girlfriend and her daughter. Prior to trial, the girlfriend executed an affidavit stating that defendant did not shoot her. At trial, the girlfriend testified that defendant was the man who shot her and that the statements in the affidavit were not true. On appeal, the court held that the trial court's order of concurrent sentences was void and that the appellate court did not err in sua sponte ordering that consecutive sentences be imposed. Consecutive sentences were mandatory under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 8/5-8-4(a) (1992) because the offenses were committed in a single course of conduct, defendant's intent did not change from one shooting to the next, he was convicted of a Class X felony, and he inflicted severe bodily injury. The statute did not violate the due process clause or the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution. The failure of defendant's attorney to use the girlfriend's prior inconsistent statements at trial was not prejudicial because the affidavit was otherwise uncorroborated and appeared to have been executed at defendant's behest during a period of reconciliation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

156 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bailey


Docket Nos. 76151, 76531 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


167 Ill. 2d 210; 657 N.E.2d 953; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 185; 212 Ill. Dec. 608



October 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 76151.--Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. William Penn, Judge, presiding.

No. 76531.--Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas Nowinski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] No. 76151--Circuit court reversed; cause remanded. No. 76531--Circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which held that the state's stalking statute, Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/121, 26-1(a)(1)(1992) was unconstitutional. In a separate action, defendant appealed his conviction under that statute and alleged that it was unconstitutional and that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction under the same. The court consolidated the two appeals.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that the stalking statute was unconstitutional because it, inter alia, was vague as to what conduct was unlawful. The statute failed to contain the language "without lawful authority," thereby ignoring that certain threats may be legal, and thus, made innocent conduct unlawful. The statute gave unfettered discretion to prosecutors in charging violations of the stalking statute. On appeal, the court disagreed and held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court reasoned that statute was not overbroad because it did not contain the language "without lawful authority." No element of protected speech was effected. Further, the statute was sufficiently clear as to what conduct was unlawful and clear standards were set forth to avoid arbitrary enforcement. Additionally, the judgment of conviction in the second action was proper because there was sufficient evidence to support that verdict.


OUTCOME: The trial court's ruling that the state stalking statute was unconstitutional was reversed, and the cause was remanded for further proceedings. The judgment of conviction in the second action was affirmed.

Admin. Office of the Ill. Courts v. State & Mun. Teamsters, Chauffeurs & Helpers, Local 726


Docket No. 75621


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


167 Ill. 2d 180; 657 N.E.2d 972; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 187; 212 Ill. Dec. 627; 150 L.R.R.M. 2935



October 19, 1995, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, administrative office of the Illinois Courts and chief circuit judges, brought an original action for a writ of prohibition pursuant to Ill. Const. art. VI, § 4(a), against respondents, Illinois Labor Relations Board (board) and local unions, to prohibit the board from considering a union representation/certification petition submitted to the board under the Illinois Public Labor Relations Act (Act), 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 315/1-27.


OVERVIEW: The board desired to proceed further with a certification petition, seeking to represent court reporters employed in the circuit courts of Illinois for collective-bargaining purposes. The union asserted that the State was the court reporters' employer and that the administrative office was the appropriate employer representative, but the board found the record insufficient to identify the court reporters' employer. The court, which subsequently stayed the administrative proceedings and granted the administrative office and judges leave to file a complaint for a writ of prohibition, granted the requested writ. In so awarding the writ, the court found the doctrine of primary jurisdiction to be inapplicable, and concluded that separation of powers concerns required that the court, as an employer of the employees at issue, not be subject to the authority of the board, an administrative agency, in a proceeding under the Act. Accordingly, the board was enjoined from proceeding further with the certification process.


OUTCOME: The court awarded the requested writ of prohibition to the administrative office of the Illinois Courts and chief circuit judges.

People v. Sims

Writ of habeas corpus denied, Judgment entered by United States ex rel. Sims v. Hulick, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 7443 (N.D. Ill., Jan. 30, 2009)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of two counts of first degree murder, two counts of armed robbery, two counts of home invasion, and one count of residential burglary, and sentenced him to death following the stabbing death of two neighbors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after various fingerprint and testimonial evidence linked defendant to an apartment in which two men had been found stabbed to death. People v. Lee


Docket No. 78085


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


167 Ill. 2d 140; 656 N.E.2d 1065; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 171; 212 Ill. Dec. 231



September 21, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. James M. Radcliffe, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which convicted defendant of one count of aggravated battery with a firearm and sentenced him to six years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The issue for the court was whether the aggravated battery with a firearm statute violated the constitutional guarantees of due process and proportionate penalties. The court held that defendant failed to persuade it that the aggravated battery with a firearm statute was not reasonably designed to remedy the evils that the legislature had selected for treatment under it. Neither was the court persuaded that designating the offense of aggravated battery with a firearm as a class X felony was cruel, degrading, or so wholly disproportionate as to shock the moral sense of the community. The legislature acted well within its broad discretion when it determined that the offense of aggravated battery with a firearm was more serious than the cited battery offenses. The aggravated battery with a firearm statute withstood defendant's constitutional challenges. The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated battery with a firearm.

Villegas v. Board of Fire & Police Comm'rs


Docket No. 77846


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


167 Ill. 2d 108; 656 N.E.2d 1074; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 175; 212 Ill. Dec. 240



September 21, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. John W. Darrah, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court reversed; circuit court reversed; board decision confirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) affirmed the decision of the trial court that Village of Downers Grove Municipal Code § 17-33(b) was unconstitutional and that plaintiff employee's due process rights were violated when he was discharged for cause. The petition of defendants, fire department officials, Village of Downers Grove, and Board of Fire and Police Commissioners, for leave to appeal was granted.


OVERVIEW: The employee falsely reported, both orally and in writing, that a fireman who injured his ankle playing basketball had injured it in the weight room by stepping on a barbell. After investigation and a determination of the facts, the fire chief notified the employee of disciplinary charges. Subsequent to a meeting with the employee, the employee's counsel, and a union representative, the fire chief discharged the employee. After a de novo evidentiary hearing, the Board of Fire and Police Commissioners ordered employee's termination. The employee alleged the village ordinance permitted evidentiary hearings for major disciplinary actions, but did not mention terminations. The village alleged it had consistently interpreted and applied its ordinance as providing terminated employees the same right of appeal as those demoted or suspended for more than three days. The court held that discharged employees were accorded the same treatment as those demoted and suspended and that the employee received due process and was not entitled to reinstatement or back pay. The employee received notice of the charges, a prediscipline opportunity to respond, and a post-termination evidentiary review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions of the appellate court and the trial court and confirmed the decision of the Board of Fire and Police Commissioners. The court held that the Downers Grove ordinance was not unconstitutional and that the employee had received due process and was afforded an adequate pretermination hearing.

People v. Hope

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of murder, attempted murder, and armed robbery. The jury found defendant eligible for the death penalty under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(b)(3) (1992). Defendant's sentence was stayed pending his direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several issues regarding the propriety of his convictions and death sentence. OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.

Village of Vernon Hills v. Vernon Fire Protection Dist. (In re Village of Vernon Hills)

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant village filed a claim against appellee fire department that challenged the constitutionality of § 14.14 of the Fire Protection District Act, 70 Ill. Comp. Stat. 705/14.14 (1992). The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) reversed the trial court's finding that the section was constitutional, and found that the section was unconstitutional. The village appealed.


OVERVIEW: A village filed a petition to disconnect certain territory served by the fire department and transfer it to a different fire department. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment that reversed the trial court's judgment in action challenging the constitutionality of the Fire Protection District Act.

Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Burt, 205 Ill. 2d 28, 792 N.E.2d 1250, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1424, 275 Ill. Dec. 477 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Burt v. McAdory, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 22548 (N.D. Ill., Dec. 16, 2003)

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County, the Hon. Lawrence A. Smith, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Stephenson County (Illinois), which, following his plea and jury findings that he was eligible for the death penalty pursuant to the multiple-murder aggravating factor, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(b)(3) (1992), and that no mitigating circumstances precluded imposition of the sentence, convicted him of two counts of first degree murder and armed robbery and sentenced him to death.

Defendant's death sentence was not arbitrary when compared to the 40-year sentence received by a codefendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Judgment & Sale of Delinquent Properties for the Tax Year 1989


Docket No. 78570


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


167 Ill. 2d 161; 656 N.E.2d 1049; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 176; 212 Ill. Dec. 215



September 21, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. S. Keith Lewis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county tax collector sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which ruled that § 16 of the Debt Reform Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 17, para. 6916 (1989), represented an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority to the county clerk.


OVERVIEW: Appellee property owners objected to certain county tax levies on the ground that the levies were adopted and presented for filing after December 31 of the tax year, the date that the county clerk was to close tax books, and hence were void. The lower court ruled in the property owners' favor. On appeal, the court held that a county clerk was permitted to accept a collection-year filing of a levy ordinance under § 16 of the Debt Reform Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 17, para. 6916 (1989). The court held that the county clerk was not thereby allowed unbounded discretion and that there was no improper delegation of legislative authority to the county clerk. The court construed § 16 to allow a governmental unit to levy a tax for the payment of bond indebtedness at any time before the bonds were issued, while permitting the county clerk to decide whether to extend the tax for the next collection when the usual time had passed for closing and delivering the tax books. As so construed, § 16 did not authorize encroachment by the county clerk into legislative processes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, finding that the tax levy statute was constitutional.

People v. Taylor


Docket No. 75277


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


166 Ill. 2d 414; 655 N.E.2d 901; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 102; 211 Ill. Dec. 518



June 22, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County, the Hon. Snyder Howell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to having committed the offense of first degree murder while committing the forcible felony of aggravated criminal sexual assault. The jury returned a verdict finding that there were not mitigating factors sufficient to preclude the imposition of the death penalty and, accordingly, the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois), sentenced him to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendant had no remorse over his raping and killing the victim and that he had been convicted as a juvenile for aggravated sexual assault. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that sentenced defendant to death and set the date of execution.

People v. Knuckles


Docket No. 73616


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


165 Ill. 2d 125; 650 N.E.2d 974; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 80; 209 Ill. Dec. 1

DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was granted post-conviction relief and allowed to withdraw her plea of guilty to her mother's murder. The state reinstated murder charges and issued two subpoenas to the psychiatrist who had examined defendant at the request of her counsel soon after the killing. The trial court sustained defendant's motion to quash and the state appealed. The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) affirmed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the psychiatrist was an agent of defense counsel and quashed the subpoenas on the basis of the attorney-client privilege and work-product doctrine, 134 Ill. The supreme court concluded that the attorney-client privilege protected communications between defendant and her nontestifying psychiatrist who was employed by defense counsel to aid in the preparation of her insanity defense. The court found that defendant did not waive the privilege by pleading insanity. The court held that there was not a generalized public interest exception to allow the state's interest in gathering evidence to overcome the attorney-client privilege.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order quashing the subpoenas.

People v. Dunigan


Docket No. 77252


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


165 Ill. 2d 235; 650 N.E.2d 1026; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 82; 209 Ill. Dec. 53



April 20, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl E. Strayhorn, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which convicted him of criminal sexual assault and sentenced him as a habitual criminal under the Habitual Criminal Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1 et seq., on the grounds that the Act was unconstitutional and it was passed in violation of the "three-readings" and "single-subject" requirements of the state constitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant received a mandatory sentence of life imprisonment as punishment for his third serious felony and his prior offenses were considered as matters in aggravation to support the sentence. The court determined that the Act did not constitute an ex post facto law or violate double jeopardy proscriptions. The court found that the legislature considered the rehabilitative potential of offenders as required by Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 by limiting the Act to offenders who had a third serious felony conviction within a prescribed period. The Act did not violate due process principles simply because it imposed a mandatory sentence. The court found that the Act did not violate the separation of powers clause of Ill. Const. art. II, § 1 even if the prosecutor had discretion in invoking the Act. The court concluded that the "enrolled-bill" rule in Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) precluded the court from inquiring into the legislature's compliance with the procedural requirements for the Act's passage. The court rejected defendant's claim that an amendment to the Act violated the single subject rule because the amendment related to a single subject, the amendment of the Criminal Code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment, which affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence of mandatory life imprisonment.

People v. Farmer


Docket Nos. 76152, 76153, 76154, 76155, 76272 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


165 Ill. 2d 194; 650 N.E.2d 1006; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 83; 209 Ill. Dec. 33; 45 A.L.R.5th 927



April 20, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Livingston County, the Hon. Charles E. Glennon, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Nos. 76152, 76153, 76154, 76272-Reversed and remanded. No. 76155-Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In four consolidated appeals, the State sought review of the declaration of the Circuit Court of Livingston County's (Illinois) that the sentencing provisions for the offense of possessing contraband in a penal institution pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/31A-1.1(b) (1992), were unconstitutional. By cross-appeal, one defendant challenged the constitutionality of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/31A-1.1(a) (1992).


OVERVIEW: In unrelated prosecutions, four defendants were charged with bringing contraband into a penal institution and for possessing contraband in a penal institution. The trial court declared that the applicable felony penalties for the offense of possessing contraband in a penal institution were unconstitutional because they violated due process guarantees under Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, and U.S. Const. amend. VIII by imposing felony penalties for an offense which required no mental state. The State sought review of the decision on grounds that the penalties applicable were justified by the magnitude of the threat which the prohibited items of contraband posed. The court reversed and remanded the case because it did not find a clear legislative purpose to impose absolute liability for possession of contraband in penal institutions. Further, the court found that knowledge was the appropriate mental state element in prosecutions under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/31A-1.1(b) (1992). Since the court concluded that the statutory scheme did not violate principles of due process, it likewise concluded that it was valid under the equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court.

People v. Rissley


Docket No. 74636


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


165 Ill. 2d 364; 651 N.E.2d 133; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 71; 209 Ill. Dec. 205



March 30, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Bureau County, the Hon. George C. Hupp, Sr., Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Bureau County (Illinois) imposed a sentence of death after defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated kidnapping and first degree murder. Defendant appealed from that judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for the kidnapping and murder of a six-year-old girl. After he pleaded guilty to the charged crimes, he filed a motion to withdraw the plea. The motion was denied. A jury found that defendant was eligible for the death penalty based on two statutory aggravating factors. The jury concluded that there were no mitigating circumstances. On appeal, the court determined that defendant was not charged with intentional or knowing murder. The court concluded that defendant was charged with felony murder. The court also determined that no double enhancement occurred because defendant's kidnapping charge was raised to an aggravated kidnapping charge based on the victim's tender age. The court held that defense counsel's comment regarding defendant's eligibility for the death penalty did not affect the fairness of the sentencing hearing. The court also held that defendant was not denied a fair and impartial jury because the trial judge did not abuse its discretion in refusing to excuse one juror or in excluding another juror. Lastly, the court held that the applicable death penalty statute was constitutional. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment imposing a death sentence on defendant following his guilty plea was affirmed.

People v. Wiley


Docket No. 71320


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


165 Ill. 2d 259; 651 N.E.2d 189; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 72; 209 Ill. Dec. 261



March 30, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Michael B. Getty, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of murder and armed robbery. Judgment was stayed pending direct appeal to the instant court. Upon review, the court found that defendant was entitled to a Batson hearing. Based on the hearing, the trial court concluded that there was no Batson violation. The instant appeal was for review of those findings as well as issues raised by defendant prior to the remand.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of three counts of murder and three counts of armed robbery. After sentencing hearings, defendant was sentenced to death on the murder convictions and consecutive 30-year sentences for the armed robbery convictions. The court affirmed the judgment and sentence. The trial court, sitting as finder of fact, properly determined that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude imposition of a sentence of death and imposed the death penalty, and properly concluded that the state had not violated the principles enunciated in Batson. Defendant was eligible for the death penalty under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(6) (1989), on the ground that the murders were committed during the course of an armed robbery. The trial court's Batson hearing focused on the state's use of peremptory challenges with respect to prospective jurors. The circumstance that state accepted some jurors who did not possess all of the ideal attributes sought by the prosecutors did not establish that the prosecution engaged in racial discrimination in its use of peremptory challenges, nor did it demonstrate a pretext for discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court sentencing defendant to be executed in a manner provided by law.

People v. Garcia


Docket No. 74980


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


165 Ill. 2d 409; 651 N.E.2d 100; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 60; 209 Ill. Dec. 172



March 23, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. John J. Nelligan, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction for first-degree murder and unlawful use of a firearm by a felon and death sentence imposed by the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: While on parole for killing her infant daughter and aggravated arson, defendant went on a drinking binge with her boyfriend. She and the boyfriend rousted her husband to get some money and she shot him. She continued drinking through the night and the next day, when she implicated her boyfriend. Taken to the police station as a ruse, the police arrested her four hours later and read her Miranda rights and she confessed. Defendant contended she was too intoxicated to understand her rights. However, her written and tape-recorded confessions did not show her to be so grossly intoxicated as not to understand her rights and she was familiar with criminal justice. Although defendant objected to the number of her peremptory challenges, she did not use all she had and was therefore not prejudiced. Some statements made to the fingerprinting officer were improperly admitted, but harmless. While defendant should have been allowed to testify about what her husband said before he was shot, whatever he said could not justify a reduction to second-degree murder. The jury was properly instructed and aggravating and mitigating evidence was properly weighed in sentencing. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because defendant received a fair trial. The date of execution was set.
