People v. Gosier


Docket No. 75742


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


165 Ill. 2d 16; 649 N.E.2d 364; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 66; 208 Ill. Dec. 308



March 23, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Harold L. Jensen, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant plead guilty to murder during the course of his jury trial in the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), and then was sentenced to death by the jury. The sentence was upheld on direct appeal. Defendant thereafter filed a post-conviction petition (725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. (1992)). The trial court denied relief without an evidentiary hearing, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to murder during his trial, and was sentenced to death by the jury. After the sentence was upheld on direct appeal, a post-conviction proceeding was brought, claiming that his guilty plea was not proper, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, and that the death penalty statute was unconstitutional. In affirming the sentence, the court held that the constitutional claim was raised and rejected on direct appeal and was res judicata. There was no showing that defendant was entitled to a new jury for good cause, so the sentencing by the original jury was proper. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to inform defendant of a right to a new jury when there was no such right, and had in fact presented the issue of defendant's troubled childhood to the jury. As defendant had vigorously attacked his guilty plea on direct appeal, and could have raised his post-conviction arguments then, the issue was waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence and set his execution date.

First Nat'l Bank v. King


Docket No. 77443


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


165 Ill. 2d 533; 651 N.E.2d 127; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 68; 209 Ill. Dec. 199



March 23, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Monica Reynolds, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant beneficiaries challenged a judgment from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's determination that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 1/2, para. 2-4(f) did not permit appellee adopted child to receive proceeds from a testamentary trust.


OVERVIEW: The testator created a trust for his children. The trust provided that after the child's death, the corpus was to be distributed per stirpes to the child's lawful descendants. The child died and one of her children also predeceased her, leaving a natural child and the adopted child. The trust filed an action for a declaratory judgment for a judicial determination as to whether the adopted child was a beneficiary under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 1/2, para. 2-4(f). The trial court's determined that the adopted child was not a beneficiary was reversed on appeal. The beneficiaries then sought review and the court affirmed. The court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 1/2, para. 2-4(f) stated that no distinction was to be drawn between adopted children and natural offspring, unless there was an intent to exclude the child. The court determined that the testator's use of the words "per stirpes" and "lawful descendants" was not enough clear and convincing evidence of an intent to exclude adopted heirs. The court held that the application of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 1/2, para. 2-4(f) did not violate the separation of powers or infringe upon the beneficiaries' due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court, which held that the trial court erred in determining that the adopted child was not a beneficiary and could not receive the proceeds of a testamentary trust.

People v. Mahaffey

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS

Northern State Home Builders Ass'n v. County of Du Page


Docket No. 76503


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


165 Ill. 2d 25; 649 N.E.2d 384; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 65; 208 Ill. Dec. 328



March 23, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Bonnie M. Wheaton, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a home builders association and others, sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) which denied their request for a declaratory judgment in their claim that alleged state statutes and local ordinances which imposed transportation impact fees on new developments were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The home builders association contended that the legislation was unconstitutional because it violated the takings clause of the United States and Illinois Constitutions and violated their right to due process. The court agreed with the association's contention concerning the legislation that imposed impact fees upon new developments to fund road improvements was unconstitutional because it did not meet the specifically and uniquely attributable test. The court noted that the legislation did not limit the use of the fees collected for road improvements made necessary by additional traffic generated by a new development. The court ruled that the forfeiture provision that penalized fee payers in the event the fee payer chose not to follow the applicable fee schedule violated the equal protection clause because it increased the fee imposed on fee payers who requested individual assessments and because the requirement bore no rational relationship to any valid state objective.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the lower court's decision that held the legislation did not violate the takings clause or the equal protection clause. The court held that legislation which did not restrict the expenditure of funds collected to deficiencies created by a new development was unconstitutional.

In re Kirchner


Docket No. 78101


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


164 Ill. 2d 468; 649 N.E.2d 324; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 56; 208 Ill. Dec. 268



February 28, 1995, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner biological father sought from the Supreme Court of Illinois a writ of habeas corpus to secure the return of his son from respondents, the adoptive parents, after the court ruled that respondents' adoption of the minor child was invalid.


OVERVIEW: While petitioner biological father was out of the country, the mother of his child decided to permit respondents, the adoptive parents, to adopt petitioner's son. Respondents and the mother convinced petitioner that his son had died, in order to prevent him from contesting the adoption. After petitioner discovered the truth, he challenged the adoption. The court invalidated the adoption, and petitioner filed for a writ of habeas corpus to obtain possession of his son. The court granted the writ. The court rejected respondents' argument that they had standing to request a custody hearing. Respondents were not entitled to a hearing under § 601(b)(2) of the Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/601(b)(2), because a nonparent could only assert standing if the natural parent did not have custody. Because petitioner had not voluntarily relinquished his rights to his child, he still had custody. Respondents were also not entitled to a hearing under an amendment to the Adoption Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/20(b) (1992), because the separation of powers doctrine, Ill. Const. of 1970 art. II, § 1, precluded retroactive application of the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner biological father a writ of habeas corpus because he was entitled to exercise control and care over his child, and respondents, the adoptive parents, were not entitled to a custody hearing under state law.

 

181 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pastewski


Docket Nos. 76447, 76518 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


164 Ill. 2d 189; 647 N.E.2d 278; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 52; 207 Ill. Dec. 316



February 17, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. William R. Penn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 76447 -- Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed. No. 76518 -- Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), reversing the trial court's application of the extended term sentencing statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2, in calculating defendants' maximum period of commitment. The appellate court held that application of the extended-term statute to defendants who have been found not guilty by reason of insanity was forbidden.


OVERVIEW: When determining the maximum period of commitment for defendants found not guilty by reason of insanity, the trial court applied the extended-term sentencing statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2, providing for an extension of commitment for one previously convicted of committing a felony. The appellate court reversed, finding that case law forbade application of the statute to defendants who had been found not guilty by reason of insanity. The court reversed the appellate court. The case upon which the appellate court relied was limited to the precise question of whether the wanton cruelty provision of the extended-term statute could apply to a defendant found not guilty by reason of insanity. Here, the court found that imposition of the extended-term statute was appropriate where the recidivist provision was based on entirely objective, historical criteria. It was in no way based on intent or any other subjective matter that conflicted with an insanity finding. Thus, there was no conflict between the successful assertion of an insanity defense and the use of the recidivism provision of the extended-term statute in determining the maximum commitment period.


OUTCOME: The order reversing the trial court's application of the extended-term sentencing statute was reversed because the appellate court erred in finding that the extended-term sentencing provisions could never be used in determining the maximum period of commitment for an insanity acquittee.

People v. Burpo


Docket No. 76424


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


164 Ill. 2d 261; 647 N.E.2d 996; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 55; 207 Ill. Dec. 503



February 17, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. James M. Radcliffe, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois). The decision resulted in the granting of a motion to dismiss a cause of action brought against defendant doctor for alleged committing various sex offenses against his patients while performing gynecological examinations.


OVERVIEW: A doctor filed a motion to dismiss charges for various sex offenses alleging the legislative scheme that defined the offense and the medical examination exception to it, made the statute void for vagueness. The circuit court granted the motion and declared the statutory scheme unconstitutionally vague. Upon review, the state argued that the doctor's arguments were based on hypothetical applications of the statute to punish innocent conduct for which the doctor was not charged. The doctor suggested that acts which constituted criminal sexual assault were committed in every gynecological exam performed thus shifting the burden to the prosecution to prove that he was entitled to a statutory medical exemption. The court held that under the statute, the prosecution had to prove not only the act of sexual penetration, but also that the doctor knew the patient did not consent. Therefore, under the statute, the burden was on the state to establish beyond a reasonable doubt what the reasonable medical standards were, that the doctor intentionally transgressed the standards, and that the patient did not consent to the transgressions. The statutory scheme was found to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court.

People v. Byron


Docket No. 72174


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


164 Ill. 2d 279; 647 N.E.2d 946; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 1; 207 Ill. Dec. 453



January 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Christy S. Berkos, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of murder, conspiracy to commit murder, home invasion, and armed robbery, and who was sentenced to death, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Among defendant's contentions on appeal he argued that he was denied his constitutional right to confront witnesses, he was denied due process of law, he was denied effective assistance of counsel, and he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Following defendant's conviction and death sentence for murder, conspiracy to commit murder, home invasion, and armed robbery, defendant appealed the judgment. Defendant argued that he was denied his constitutional right to confront witnesses against him, he was denied due process of law by comments the prosecutor made during closing argument, and he was denied effective assistance of counsel. The court affirmed, holding that defendant waived any objection to the admission of the testimony by failing to properly preserve the issue for review. Additionally, the court held that neither plain error or ineffective assistance of counsel existed. Further, the court found that defendant was not substantially prejudiced by the prosecutor's closing arguments. The court reasoned that the prosecutor's remarks were brief, isolated, and came after the jury had already heard an abundance of evidence regarding the defendant's guilt. Further, the court held that defendant was represented by skilled, conscientious, defense counsel. The court concluded that there was no reason to question the jury's judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting and sentencing defendant to death for murder, conspiracy to commit murder, home invasion, and armed robbery was affirmed because defendant waived his objection regarding his right to confront witnesses, defendant was not substantially prejudiced by the prosecutor's closing arguments, and defendant was represented by skilled, conscientious defense counsel. The court found no reason to question the jury's judgment.

185 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carrillo


Docket Nos. 76395, 7664 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


164 Ill. 2d 144; 646 N.E.2d 582; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 4; 207 Ill. Dec. 16



January 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas A. Hett, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Having been previously convicted of lesser charges arising out of the same circumstances, defendants were indicted for murder. Defendants sought dismissal on double jeopardy grounds. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) reversed the trial court, holding that all of the indictments were barred except for that of murder based upon a strong probability of death or great bodily harm. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that in cases where double jeopardy might otherwise be implicated, an exception exists where the state is initially unable to proceed on the more serious charge because the additional facts necessary to sustain that charge have not yet occurred. Thus the felony murder and intentional murder charges faced by defendants were not barred by the double jeopardy clause because defendants could not have been prosecuted for the murder until the victim's death. Further, the first defendant's guilty plea did not implicate the collateral estoppel component of double jeopardy. However, the other defendant had already been acquitted of attempted murder, aggravated battery and armed robbery. Thus there was reasonable doubt that that she had the requisite intent to kill or to cause great bodily harm or commit armed robbery. Consequently, the murder charges based upon intent to kill or do great bodily harm were foreclosed as to her. The murder counts based upon knowledge that the shooting created a strong probability of death or great bodily harm were constitutional as against both defendants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the appellate court. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the cause. As regards the second defendant, she could not be charged with felony murder based upon armed robbery or based upon murder based upon the intent to kill or cause great bodily harm.

Church v. State


Docket No. 76583


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


164 Ill. 2d 153; 646 N.E.2d 572; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 8; 207 Ill. Dec. 6



January 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Menard County, the Hon. M. Carol Pope, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; Department decision set aside; circuit court judgment reversed; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant challenged the decision of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which upheld the action of appellee department in denying his application for a private alarm contractor's license.


OVERVIEW: The applicant had purchased a private alarm contracting business and began operating the business on a part-time basis. He learned that the Private Detective, Private Alarm and Private Security Act of 1983 (Act), 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. 445/1 et seq. (1992), required him to obtain a license from the department before engaging in the private alarm contracting business. On appeal of denial of the application, the court reversed and remanded. The appellate court improperly determined that denial of the application was a proper exercise of discretionary authority under the Act. The court concluded that Ill. Comp. Stat. 445/14(c) (1992), as interpreted by the department, unconstitutionally granted members of the private alarm contracting trade an unregulated a monopoly over entrance into the private alarm contracting trade. While statutory experience requirements in the Act were invalid, it did not lead to the conclusion that the applicant was entitled to a license. Thus, the court simply reversed the department's finding that the applicant was not qualified to take the licensure examination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

People v. Lewis


Docket No. 72308


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


165 Ill. 2d 305; 651 N.E.2d 72; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 9; 209 Ill. Dec. 144

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County, which following a jury trial, convicted him of murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(2) (1985), and armed robbery under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18-2(a). Defendant was found eligible for the death penalty with no mitigating facts sufficient to preclude death. Defendant was sentenced to death on the murder conviction, and to imprisonment for the armed robbery conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised over 25 issues on appeal. The court held that the trial court's refusal to "life qualify" prospective jurors during the death sentence hearing denied his right to due process and vacated the sentence. The court held that defendant was not entitled to a continuance due to the State's late disclosure of the psychiatric records of a key witness. The court held that although there were several evidentiary issues that, had they been properly raised should have resulted in the exclusion of evidence, none were such that they denied defendant of a fair trial. The court held that there was sufficient evidence of the robbery claim, because even though the victim was unable to resist, resistance was not a necessary element in proving robbery. After addressing several of defendant's arguments the court held that any error committed in the jury instructions was harmless error. The court held that evidence that implied that defendant engaged in prior criminal activity should not have been admitted, and the fact that such evidence came to the jury by way of inference did not alter its potentially prejudicial character. However the court found no undue prejudice as a result.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both convictions and the sentence for the armed robbery, but vacated the death sentence and remanded the matter to the trial court for a new death sentence hearing.

 

189 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jeffries


Docket Nos. 75161, 75647 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


164 Ill. 2d 104; 646 N.E.2d 587; 1995 Ill. LEXIS 11; 207 Ill. Dec. 21



January 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 75161 - Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas A. Hett, Judge, presiding.

No. 75647 - Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Ralph Reyna, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 75161 -- Affirmed. No. 75647 -- Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in unrelated trials of first degree murder. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed. Defendants' appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that the second degree murder statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2(c) (1987), was unconstitutional because it required them to prove mitigating factors. The appellate court held that defendants were not required to prove any element of the first degree murder they were charged with, therefore there was no violation of due process. The court affirmed. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2(a) (1987) required that the state first prove beyond a reasonable doubt all elements of the offense of first degree murder as defined in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 (1987). A first degree murder charge would be reduced to second degree murder only where the state had proven the elements of first degree murder and defendant had established a mitigating factor by a preponderance of the evidence. Defendant was not required to prove his innocence. Under the imperfect self-defense theory, defendants were not forced to argue that their "belief was unreasonable." Rather, defendants were required to prove, by a preponderance of the evidence, that they had an actual belief in the necessity of self-defense, and that their belief in the necessity of self-defense was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the constitutionality of the Illinois homicide scheme for first and second degree murder and affirmed the judgments of the appellate court.

 

190 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wilson


Docket No. 73903


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


164 Ill. 2d 436; 647 N.E.2d 910; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 172; 207 Ill. Dec. 417



December 22, 1994, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Mclean County, the Hon. W. Charles Witte, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the death sentence imposed by the Circuit Court of Mclean County (Illinois) following defendant's conviction for murder and armed robbery. Defendant alleged that the trial court impermissibly admitted certain statements made by him into evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for murder and armed robbery and the trial court's imposition of the death penalty. The court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court found that the trial court permissibly allowed defendant's statements into evidence because the defendant was not a suspect when he made the statements at the crime scene. The court held that defendant's second written statement was admissible because defendant had waived his Miranda rights prior to the statement. Once defendant voluntarily waived his rights, the statement was admissible. The court held that the trial court's decision to deny defendant's motion to suppress the statements he made to police was not clearly erroneous. The court determined that defendant's statements to a mental health provider were admissible because he was not a suspect at the time and because the statements fell under the homicide exception of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 810(a)(9) (1991). The court found that the trial court's determination that the aggravation evidence outweighed the mitigation evidence was supported by the record and affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for armed robbery and murder and the imposition of the death penalty. The court found that the statements made by defendant and admitted into evidence were permissible because defendant made the statements voluntarily.

 

191 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harris


Docket No. 73899


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


164 Ill. 2d 322; 647 N.E.2d 893; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 174; 207 Ill. Dec. 400



December 22, 1994, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. William J. Hibbler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of one count each of murder, attempted murder, and aggravated battery and of two counts of attempted armed robbery and sentenced him to death on the murder conviction and imprisonment on the remaining felonies, on the grounds that the State excluded minority members from his jury.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the trial judge's determination that the State's explanations for peremptory challenges were sufficiently race-neutral was not clearly erroneous. A juror's friendship with a city council member and a juror's failure to candidly disclose her spouse's occupation were sufficient grounds for peremptory challenges. Although the State's assumption that a juror lived close to the murder scene was incorrect, it was not necessary that the State establish the empirical truth of its explanation as long as the prosecutor reasonably believed it to be true. Exercising a peremptory challenge to leave room for the selection of more favorable jurors was also a race-neutral explanation and was not clearly pretextual where the challenge was sustainable on other grounds. The court found that the unemployment of a juror's spouse could be considered in combination with other circumstances in exercising a peremptory challenge. The court determined that the sentencing judge's adoption of the eligibility determination made at the original sentencing hearing was sufficient to constitute an express finding that defendant acted with intent or knowledge in causing the victim's death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and directed the clerk of court to enter an order setting the date on which the sentence of death was to be carried out.

 

192 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. McCauley


Docket No. 73800


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


163 Ill. 2d 414; 645 N.E.2d 923; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 175; 63 U.S.L.W. 2476; 206 Ill. Dec. 671



December 22, 1994, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged, by way of interlocutory appeal, a judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) upholding the trial court's grant of defendant's motion to suppress evidence of statements and a lineup identification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was brought to the police in connection with a shooting death but did not ask for a lawyer. However, an attorney came to the police station, identified himself as defendant's attorney, and asked to speak with defendant. The police refused and declined to tell defendant that attorney was present. Then, defendant was placed in a lineup and a witness identified him. Defendant was indicted for first-degree murder. On review from the granting of defendant's suppression motion, the court held that state constitutional guarantees did not permit police to delude custodial suspects, exposed to interrogation, into falsely believing they were without immediately available legal counsel and to also prevent that counsel from accessing and assisting their clients during the interrogation. The court also found that there was no question that adversary judicial proceedings had not been initiated at the time of the lineup, thus, defendant was not entitled to the assistance of counsel. The court further held that as the lineup identification was not the fruit of police misconduct, there could be no basis to suppress evidence of the lineup identification.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the trial court's order suppressing any statements defendant made after his attorney was present at the station and refused access to him. The judgment was reversed as to the trial court's order suppressing evidence of the lineup identification of defendant.

 

193 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Barger v. Peters


Docket No. 76945


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


163 Ill. 2d 357; 645 N.E.2d 175; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 179; 206 Ill. Dec. 170



December 22, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, two inmates, filed a class action against appellant, the director of the Department of Corrections (director), for the change in the law that made them ineligible for increased credit. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted a permanent injunction that prohibited the director from applying the law to the inmates as a class. The director appealed.


OVERVIEW: As of 1990, prisoners were allowed to increase their good-conduct credit. Public Act 88-311, effective in 1993, amended Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1003-6-3 (1991), so as to exclude prisoners from their previous opportunities to increase good-conduct credit. Because Public Act 88-311 made the inmates ineligible for increased credit, they brought a class action against the director. The trial court ruled that Public Act 88-311 violated ex post facto prohibitions under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and Ill. Const. 1970 art. I, § 16, and it enjoined the director from applying it to the inmates. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the federal and the state constitutions prohibited the state from enacting any ex post facto law. The court adopted a generous understanding of the term "punishment" and held that the elimination of opportunities to increase good-conduct credit was a change in the punishment associated with a crime and resulted in greater punishment. Public Act 88-311 thus violated the ex post facto prohibitions as to those inmates who had committed their crimes after 1990 but who were deprived of the opportunity to earn increased good-conduct credit in 1993.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the permanent injunction entered by the trial court that precluded application of a public act to persons who committed the offenses for which they were convicted on and after September 10, 1990, to and including August 10, 1993.

Fields Jeep-Eagle v. Chrysler Corp.


Docket Nos. 74151, 75293, 75323, 75358 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


163 Ill. 2d 462; 645 N.E.2d 946; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 170; 206 Ill. Dec. 694



December 22, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John N. Hourihane, and the Hon. Richard L. Curry, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, appellant dealerships and intervenor-appellant Secretary of State sought review of the judgments of the Circuit Courts of Cook County (Illinois), which held that §§ 4(e)(8) and 12(c) of the Motor Vehicle Franchise Act, codified at 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 710/4(e)(8), 12(c) (1992), were unconstitutional in that they delegated administrative and executive functions to the judiciary.


OVERVIEW: The dealerships brought an action against appellee franchisers and relocating franchises to prevent the relocation of other dealership franchises into their respective market areas. The franchisers and relocating franchises contended that §§ 4(e)(8) and 12(c) of the Motor Vehicle Franchise Act (Act), codified at 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 710/4(e)(8), 12(c) (1992), were unconstitutional in that they delegated administrative and executive functions to the judiciary and that dismissal was proper. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court concluded that the investigation into and weighing of the statutory and nonstatutory factors in order to decide whether a dealership should be established or relocated, and what the public interest and welfare was in each case involving a proposed dealership, were not functions that the courts were equipped to perform nor which the legislature could constitutionally require them to perform. Sections 4(e)(8) and 12(c) violated the of the separation of powers and due process principles expressed in Ill. Const. art. II, § 1 (1970) because the Act was unconstitutionally vague and it impermissibly delegated non-judiciary function to the courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

195 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kimbrough


Docket No. 75408


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


163 Ill. 2d 231; 644 N.E.2d 1137; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 151; 206 Ill. Dec. 84



November 23, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James Zafiratos, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the indictment charging defendant with violations of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, 720 Ill. Cons. Stat. § 570/100 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the unlawful delivery of 100 segregated parts of a substance containing LSD in violation of § 401(a)(7)(A)(ii) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act (Act), 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 570/401(a), and with unlawful possession of 100 segregated parts of a substance containing LSD. The trial court found portions of the Act unconstitutional. The court reversed and remanded the dismissal of the indictment against defendant. Defendant's argument that the LSD provisions violated equal protection because the classifications arising from the grams/objects distinction were not rationally related to the purpose of the Act was without merit. The legislature's decision to differentiate punishment based on liquid versus carrier form was constitutional because LSD was normally used and distributed in an object/carrier form, and the legislature could reasonably have determined that LSD reduced to the carrier form was more dangerous to the public health and safety than pure, liquid LSD. The Act did not violate due process because an accused will never be subjected to a more severe penalty for possession than for delivery.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded dismissal of the indictment charging defendant with violations of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act (Act). The Act did not violate equal protection or due process. The legislature had a proper basis for differentiating punishment based on liquid versus carrier form, as the legislature could reasonably have determined that LSD reduced to the carrier form was more dangerous to than liquid LSD.

People v. Hickman


Docket Nos. 76225, 76226, 76227, 76228, 76751 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


163 Ill. 2d 250; 644 N.E.2d 1147; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 154; 206 Ill. Dec. 94



November 23, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. Barry E. Pulkin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted defendants' motion to dismiss the criminal drug conspiracy charges and declared that the sentencing provision of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/405.1 (1992) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with criminal drug conspiracy under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/405.1 (1992). Each defendant asked the trial court to dismiss the criminal drug conspiracy charge and declare that the sentencing provision of the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The trial court so ruled. The court reversed and held that 570/405.1 provides fair warning of the possible penalty. It unambiguously notified a person of common intelligence that if he or she was convicted of criminal drug conspiracy, that person could be imprisoned or fined or both, from zero up to the maximum sentence for the offense that was the object of the conspiracy. The court found that it could have provided letter-perfect notice had it specified a minimum penalty; However, that was not a constitutional requirement. Further, the court stated that the availability of different punishments for separate offenses based on the same act did not offend due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the criminal drug conspiracy charges against defendants and its determination that the statute was unconstitutional.

People v. C.R.H. (In re C.R.H.)


Docket No. 76377


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


163 Ill. 2d 263; 644 N.E.2d 1153; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 155; 206 Ill. Dec. 100



November 23, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, the Hon. Timothy R. Gill, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Second District, Illinois, which reversed a circuit court's order adjudicating appellee minor delinquent because his mother was not given notice of the juvenile proceedings and the circuit court did not have jurisdiction, and held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 801-15(b) (705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/1-15(b)) was unconstitutional because it infringed upon due process.


OVERVIEW: The state filed an amended supplemental petition for an adjudication of the minor's delinquency in connection with several offenses, and the petition listed his mother's address, while his father's address was unknown and his father did not respond to notice by publication. His mother attended prior juvenile court proceedings, but was not served with a summons and was not present at the arraignment and detention, adjudicatory, or dispositional hearings. The minor was adjudged a delinquent and committed to the department of corrections. The appellate court held that the circuit court did not have jurisdiction because the mother did not receive notice as required by due process, and found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 801-15(b) (705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/1-15(b)) unconstitutionally conflicted with the notice requirement. On further appeal, the court found that the notice requirement could not be waived unknowingly and unintentionally, while the statute required the minor to object to lack of parental notice prior to the start of the hearing or waive the right to assert it either at the hearing or on appeal. The court noted that its rules prevailed over a conflicting statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court and agreed with its finding that the statute was unconstitutional because it impermissibly resulted in the waiver of the right of the minor and his parents to due process.

The Chicago Bar Ass'n v. Department of Revenue


Docket No. 77420


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


163 Ill. 2d 290; 644 N.E.2d 1166; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 160; 206 Ill. Dec. 113



November 23, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bar association challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed appellee department of revenue's ruling that its headquarters were not exempt from real estate taxes under § 19.1 of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 500.1 (1991).


OVERVIEW: A bar association claimed that its headquarters were exempt from real estate taxes under ch. 120, para. 500.1 because it was adjacent to a school. The department denied the exemption. The lower court affirmed the department's decision and declared the portion of ch. 120, para. 500.1 exempting from taxation real property adjacent to school grounds invalid. The court affirmed. It held that although the lower court should not have declared ch. 120, para. 500.1 to be facially invalid, its judgment upholding the department's decision was correct. The adjacent property clause in ch. 120, para. 500.1 did not modify the limitations imposed by Ill. Const. art. IX, § 6. It provided a description of a type of property that could have been entitled to exemption. The bar association was a professional organization whose headquarters served primarily as a place where its members could meet and dine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the department's ruling that the bar association's headquarters were not exempt from real estate taxes.

Sepmeyer v. Holman


Docket No. 75904


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


162 Ill. 2d 249; 642 N.E.2d 1242; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 150; 205 Ill. Dec. 125



October 27, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County, the Hon. J. Lawrence Keshner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate appealed from a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which reversed a trial court order dismissing on statute of limitations grounds a wrongful death action filed by plaintiff estate administrator under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-202.1.


OVERVIEW: Eleven years after a murder, and after being notified of a money judgment for the inmate convicted of the crime in an unrelated civil action, the administrator of the decedent's estate filed a wrongful death action against the inmate under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-202.1, which allowed any action for damages to be brought against certain felons without regard to the statute of limitations. The trial court found that § 13-202.1 did not apply retroactively and dismissed the administrator's wrongful death action because it was untimely under the applicable two-year statute of limitations. While the appeal was pending, the Illinois Legislature amended § 13-202.1 to expressly revive time-barred claims against murderers and to apply the statute retroactively. The appellate court reversed the trial court's order and held that the amendment effectively revived the administrator's wrongful death claim. In the subsequent appeal, the court reversed and held that the Illinois Constitution precluded the legislature from expressly reviving a claim previously barred by the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment reversing the trial court's order dismissing on statute of limitations grounds a wrongful death action against the inmate filed by the estate administrator. The court held that the Illinois Constitution precluded the Illinois Legislature from expressly reviving a claim previously barred by the statute of limitations.

FDIC v. O'Malley


Docket No. 76106


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


163 Ill. 2d 130; 643 N.E.2d 825; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 147; 205 Ill. Dec. 534



October 27, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied December 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas E. Hoffman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guarantor challenged the decision of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed in part the decision that entered judgment in favor of appellee Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation (FDIC), in its corporate capacity, but reduced the award of interest in an action brought against the guarantor to enforce a guarantee signed by him in connection with a bank loan.


OVERVIEW: The FDIC, in its corporate capacity, brought an action against a guarantor to enforce a guarantee in connection with a bank loan. The trial court held in favor of the FDIC, and the guarantor appealed. The lower appellate court affirmed in part but reduced the award of interest, and an appeal was taken. On appeal, the court held that: 1) the guarantor waived the issue of judicial disqualification pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 63(C)(1)(c) (113 Ill. 2d Rev. 63 (C)(1)(c)) where the trial judge disclosed, prior to trial, that he had previously represented the FDIC as a receiver for the lender but the guarantor did not pursue the matter further until an unfavorable judgment was entered against him; and 2) the guarantor could not rely upon a separate release agreement that did not strictly comply with statutory codification of the D'Oench, Duhme doctrine, even though terms of the guarantee allowed the debtor to cancel upon written notice, absent evidence that the guarantor gave such notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision which entered judgment in favor of the FDIC but reduced the award of interest in an action brought against the guarantor to enforce a guarantee signed by him in connection with a bank loan.
